### Room altars 
- [[2025-10-19]] from [[2025-10 Cedric and Romane Immersion]]
	- having 4 places in the room, each place with be one aspect, for example: 
		- steps, headmovements, hips, bodymovements
		- the closer we are to some point, the more we have to express with this tool. If we are in the middle, we express with everything. 
		- Can be used also for different aspects of music as we did at [[Dancing the layers of music (with room separation)]]

Ze [[2024-12 Prague Zoukmass]]

# Workshops

# Exercises
*Idea from [[2025-09 Zouktime Croatia]] when dancing with [[Romane Leterme]]*: 
CviÄenÃ­ na headmovementy - pomoci partnerce napnout ruce a celÃ© tÄ›lo co nejvÃ­c nahoru a potom pustit. Jakmile pustÃ­me, tak uvolnit napÄ›ti do headmovement pozice. Je moÅ¾nÃ© zkouÅ¡et pozici hlavy vzadu nebo na boku. DÅ¯leÅ¾itÃ© je, aby partnerka nezkolabovala, drÅ¾ela si vlastnÃ­ tÄ›lo, ale zÃ¡roveÅˆ se snaÅ¾ila uvolnit a povolit energii projÃ­t dolÅ¯. DÃ¡ se potom napojit na moÅ¾nost tohle navÃ©st - jdeme z napnutÃ© pozice, ale v uzavÅ™enÃ©m hrudnÃ­ku. 

Playing with the position of "high five" in basic step. With proper elasticity we can lead many things. 
Things that are neccessary for this: 
- knowing how to react with your frame on recieved pressure (returning it back) even when it increases during some step

When leaders are leading F back, they create the movement more with their legs than frame, the frame is just releasing the tension as a spring.

Options: 
- turn of the follower to the left and right, lead with hand
- turn of the follower with left or right inwards or outwards with pushing unequally to one side
- changing the direction ([[PÅ™evedenÃ­]]), can be also added the inward turn (I saw it teaching [[Michal ChromÄÃ¡k]] in lamba)
- building pressure and then releasing into calmness (back step for follower)
### Exercise for musicality
We set up some parts of songs that leaders stop at. Then the lady says what she feels there in the music. The leader has to do it. Then we change ladies and repeat just with another part of the song. The leader can dance whatever in between. 
Can be connected with topic planning the musicality emphasis

### Explanation for how we express music
Connect the way we can sing rhythm of one word in song to way we express musicality.

### Idea from dancing with Julia Utig. 
Trying to play with the limit positions. Always somehow get your partner into disbalance and going into the biggest limit (with a lot of control and slowly) and then create something out of it. Trying to lose the fear of imbalance. 

### Exercise for Musicality
People are dancing on some song and I am stopping the music randomly. When I stop they have to stop at the last step and make the movement super Slow motion so they never stop moving.
### Communicating the inspiration
In couples, one couple is dancing, second one is looking, after minute or so, they tell to the couple who was dancing, what they are doing and how they are dancing (what is inspiring for them or what they like). Try to be observing, not judging. 
### Taking inspiration during dancing from other leader
- splitting them into two couples
- one couple makes one 8 (or 2 if it makes sence like boomerang) and stops, the second couple has to repeat their movement
- once the second couple is finished, the first one can go again
- first start without music or on some lyrical song

# 0_Dance philosophy and ideas.md

---
up:
  - "[[0_Dance MOC]]"
specification:
---
[[My dance philosophy]]


**Also we can imagine that the steps are single piano keys. When we push multiple keys, it creates a chord - that is for us a dance element (like [[Basic step]]). But the single element can have many variations like chords, we can add some more steps or slightly change the ones we use. We can play very strong or very silent. After every chord there is a number of other chords that fit in (not infinity options). Some that are very elegant, some that are a bit harder to understand and some very unusually progressions. [^6]**

If you wait to hear the beat to start to dance, you will always be late [^6]

Leaders need flexible mind and flexible body to be able to react  ([[Xandy Liberato]] on [[2022-04 Zouk Bootcamp with Xandy]])

When you dance, you can enjoy the luxury of being you. [^2] 

Don't try to dance as you see it. Rather, try to see and deconstruct the movement and feel how is it pleasant for your body (listen to your body).  Usually the movement is not as big as you see it (especially with head movements). [^1]

We all have our own journey, everyone is developing at their own pace [^3]

Don't exchange the idea of control for trust. [^5]

Tam, kam dÃ¡te pozornost, tam proudÃ­ energie. 

> [!QUote] Quotes from [[Jerry Lai]] [^4]
> Do not mistake our progress in learning some skill (dance) for our self worth 
> 
> Watch yourself for signs of addiction. Do you NEED to dance, or do you WANT to dance? Is it negatively affecting other parts of your life that you want to keep?
> 
> Having a great dance connection doesn't mean anything other than that. Asking is sexy. Don't assume.
> 
> Ask your teachers WHY, and use their answers to determine what you keep. Seek curious teachers that are forever student
> 
> 1:1 Ratio for Learning : Integrating. You'll never watch those videos you took half-assedly... so spend the better to practice/integrating it into the body right after.
> 
> It's going to be a lesson on LETTING GO. You have no control over anything other than your own body and your reactions. The sooner you realize that the happier you will be.
> 
> Teaching is one of the most effective forms of learning that you can do.
> 
> Cross-train. A lot of the problems you're having are not solved through more Brazilian Zouk classes. Mobility. Yoga. Rock-climbing. Movement. Strength Training. Contemporary. Tai Chi. Gaga.

# 0_General topics Social dance.md

## Feedback
Leaders make something on purpose (for example holding the hands too tight) and followers duty is to just say out loud to his face "you are hurting me, this is a bit too much". We can try this with multiple situations - also with setting up the boundaries inside of a dance and hug. 

## Closeness

Remember the rule of 90/10 - you are offering the space to a lady by coming to a 90% distance and she needs to fill in those 10%

# Balance.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
technique:
principle:
  - "[[Weight transfer and footwork]]"
---

When your upper body is in the limit of your foot, it is much harder to lose your balance. [^1]

When shifting weight, make sure you are not putting your weight on the knees but on the pelvic floor. [^2]

The body is always searching for balance. What changes is how much tension we add, helping that search. Too much tension makes it harder for body to adjust. 
Most of the time when we are learning dance we don't "lose" balance in the strict sense - we interfere with our ability to recover it.
When our body is out off balance (when the center of gravity moves outside of base of support), body actively works to restore it and seeks equilibrium. 

> [!NOTE] In this way, being "off balance" is better described as being in *state of correction*.

Falling occurs when the body's corrective capacity is exceeded. Many dance teachers frame it as *extension of balance*: the body moves through imbalance and reorganizes upon impact or recovery.

# Beauty in dance.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
---



The first factor I will call EMBODIMENT. It is the way your body moves at any time as the result of your personal history, your life, your activities and your psychological state. Your body has grown into your current life much like a tree adapts itself to the surrounding conditions. In Western Europe, for example, most tango people have intellectual background and their professional activities demand to sit long hours in front of a computer. Such a lifestyle results in a tense shoulder area, forward protrusion of the head, inflexible pelvis and weak legs: just about the opposite of what is needed in dance.

You cannot be tense and move sensually. You cannot be tense and dance elegantly, or play, or make love with abandonment. Tension is not only the opposite of movement: it is also the opposite of joy

Your embodiment is further defined by your psychological state, your sense of self as a unique separate human being. As Alan Watts wrote â€œI have discovered that the ego is a chronic and habitual sense of muscular strainâ€. A lot of tension in our muscles is the result of our ego-related anxieties. Mindfulness meditation or simply being in a happy mood makes your body more relaxed because you loosen up the tightness inside yourself that you unconsciously associate with this feeling of â€œmeâ€ and what this â€œmeâ€ represents.

The more you move in awareness of how you move, the more you will improve the way you move, and the better you move, the better you will feel physically and mentally.

A beautifully moving body is naturally toned, holds itself upright without effort, finds balance easily, its posture and gait are anatomically efficient, its movements are smooth and harmonious. Such a body is highly reactive, spontaneously adequate in its reactions and generally relaxed, meaning it is free of tension. Tension is the opposite of movement and therefore the enemy of dance. If one part of your body is holding itself in a tensed position during the dance it will spoil the visual impression, no matter how masterful you are in your steps

beautiful dancer also keeps his or her energy flowing. This does not mean you should be visibly moving all the time, but even when you are standing completely still you should â€œcontinue to vibrateâ€, as one of my ballet teachers said. â€œYou can always tell a dancer who vibrates from one who is just standing there.â€

Beautiful dance looks like flying, not like moving furniture

A beautiful movement is one that makes meaningful lines in space. This means that each movement has a certain given trajectory, logical within the whole. Dance is what happens while you are creating those lines with your body and it comes down to HOW you create them. Making beautiful lines means completing each movementâ€™s trajectory fully. [^1]

When in despair, remind yourself that aesthetics do not just happen, they need to be trained

PRESENCE. You can always tell when a dancer is working hard, stressing about the result, executing a routine or when s/he is truly dancing. â€œBecomingâ€ dance is what ultimately dance is all about and it means to be fully present in what your body is doing, at once being the dancer and letting the dance happen through you. For this you will need to concentrate your full attention every time on here and now and completely, consciously, abandon yourself to the dance. If


[^1]: Some Tango article long gone

# Bounce in dance.md

---
notetoolbar: General
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
connected_with:
---


We use bounce mostly with songs that have harder pulse on 1 and 3. Lifts with our bodies are also on 1 and 3. 

Songs that are inviting bounce: 
- [[Kakah - Estillo tropical]]
- [[Hedegaard - Ganja Gun]]
- [[Puri, Valeria Sandoval, Mikey Dinero - Cola]]

# Chest torsion (rotation).md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Principles of leading and following]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Leading in zouk]]"
  - "[[Following in zouk]]"
---


# Helpful exercises 
One partner is holding hips. Other partner is rotating chest from one side to another, slowly and steadily. Concentrating on breath.

# Classes/2024-01 Lui and Larissa Headmovement week.md

---
teacher:
  - "[[Lui and Larrisa]]"
---

# Class 1
You can organize headmovements only into three movements: 
- Roasted chicken
- balao
- tilted turns
But what about side to side chocique and toalha

### Balao 
mixture of flexion and extension of spine (down and up) and lateral movement of spine side to side, together it is a circumdiction of spine.
First we have to create some strech in our spine and then relax it (instead of collapsing), so there should be any flaps of our skin. If we have space in our spine with stretch, it is safe to do headmovements
> you should always have similar feeling like when you are standing straight even when doing headmovements

How to start balao:
1) start side to side inclination with our chest (we can think about having our head on more horizontal level)
2) keeping the chest in the same place, closing it and opening it
3) Doing circle
If I don't use chest going back, I will use the flexibility only of my neck. Using more mobility of our chest

When we are opening chest, we can think about someone puhing the middle of our back forward, not bringing our shoulderblades together
#### Leading 
When leading balao, Lui showed example on plate (her shoulder line) and apple rolling around (head of follower)

### Tilted turns
- We usually use the higher shoulder (that is the easier) if the turn is without holding the hand (just contact on shoulder). Usually we are pushing with the turn
- when the head is forward usually we use the shoulder in the outside of the rotation

Balao - tilted turn - Balao (turns with connection on F shoulders)
- most common is doing it with head tilted on the side and continue with balao the same direction as the turn
- but it can be done in either direction and with head in any position (it is just harder and needs more clarity of leading)


Headmovement and body rotation in the same direction = toalha
Headmovement and body rotation in different direction = grilled chicken

# Class 2
In turns in spot we often use footwork Replacing footwork.
1) Moove your foot to the direction of your turn
![[Pasted image 20240112111003.png]] 
2) replace the original place of the first foot
![[Pasted image 20240112111014.png]]

Lui says, its the same like when someone calls you from some direction, then your feet do this automatically.

Second idea of footwork is Paddle footwork (also for stationary turns but for higher speed)
- one base leg that does not move from one place
- second feet is paddling on the floor without transfering the weight
Base leg the weight is on the front so it could turn
we are trying to paddle less and less, to train our balance

## Displacement turns - Chanes turns (from [[Balet]]) - postupnÃ© toÄky do prostoru
- every step half of a turn (jako kruÅ¾Ã­tko)
- we can choose how far appart are the legs
- they are saying - imageine that you walk like a penguine (we say kruÅ¾Ã­tko)
- it's good to look at the direction you are going (spotting)

Leaders are on a side of follower, looking in the direction we are going.
The more displacement you have, the further apart are legs, if the rotation is bigger than displacement, then the feet are closer apart

These turns can be led also around the leader. 
When the rotation of the turn and the revolution (rotace kolem leadera) are opposite direction, it is easier for the follower because she doesn't have to turn 180 degrees but less

## Type of frames
### Manequine frame
in [[Lateral]] etc
- elbows little forward in front of the body
- its similar position of when you sit down, where your hands are comfortable
the higher are the elbows, the more engagement I want, the more tension I am giving.

### Roof frame 
(viz [[Lui and Larrisa headmovement Masterclass]])

### How to break frame
1) using the inertia of the body (for example in [[Dance/Elements/Open to the right]]) - it would be too hard to keep the frame in that moment
2) changing the angle of hands
3) if I bring the hands into "empty zone" (center of the body of the follower)

Pleasant positions of frame for headmovement
In the manequine frane With tilt to the side - 45 degrees
![[Pasted image 20240112170116.png|200]]

With the inclination backwards, hands are around shoulders height of the follower
![[Pasted image 20240112170228.png]]

Also when going up and down, the hands are going a little bit towards the body of F (because the distance shortens)

If there is a lot of space from the leader, follower can choose to use more inertia of the movement (keeping the flow of energy through her body). If there are constantly some information from leader, it is not easy.

In tilted turns, the hand of the leader is on the opposite side of the head of F


---

# Classes/Lui and Larissa - Counterbalance masterclass.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance class
  - zouk
  - online class
teacher:
  - "[[Lui and Larrisa]]"
date_start: 2024-11-05
level: 
notetoolbar: Zouk
elements:
  - "[[Contrabalance]]"
---
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FCFeN20uHu8&t=1367s&ab_channel=DanceUni

colgado - counterbalance pose from [[tango argentino]]
they learned a lot of tango techniques of counterbalance

## Definitions  
Colgado (hanging)
- closer bases, further body, connection by traction

Volcada (leaning)
- horizontal force interaction
- far bases, closer body
- connection by compression

Planeio / Planada (flow)
- body on top of the base
- mixed adjustment connection

Lifting
- vertical force interaction
- one partner is lifting the other one

## Other
When you are closer to the center, your angular speed is bigger, because you have smaller distance, but same speed as your partner


## Ways of offering our body weight for countrabalance
![[Lui and Larissa - Counterbalance masterclass-20241106172958772.jpg]]
Sitting
- vertical alignment from head to hips
Cambret 
- upper body gives countrabalance
Leaning
- body aligned straight from head to toes

Stable balance
- when external forces are aligned with the countrabalance (so for example your hips are always returning to the right positions)
- **this is what we try to have**

Unstable balance
- external forces are trying to force you into different position

If F wants to increase to weight she gives to the follower, she moves the opposite direction as the leader. If you want to decrease, you move closer to the partner. 

Follower can accelerate/deccelarate by moving lateral inclination. If she leans to the same direction as she is turning, it will speed up.
![[Lui and Larissa - Counterbalance masterclass-20241106173852681.jpg|437]]

Leaders:
every time you are in your back foot, you are in the acceleration paddle, in the front foot it is your brake

The distance of leaders foot towards the followers foot will influence a lot the acceleration. When you put back foot further away it means more acceleration, if you put front foot futher, it means slower. But it is not a distance away from them, but paralell! If I move away, I just reduce the amount of counterbalance.

If I want more speed I can either go more steps and faster or every two steps I increase the amount of rotation (angluar amplitude). They recommend to practise the angular amplitude. 

If I want to decelerate, I can spend more time on my front foot or increase the distance. The same with acceleration. 

![[Lui and Larissa - Counterbalance masterclass-20241106174228700.jpg]]

# Second lesson
â¯ [Masterclass 2 video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mXM2AcP21r0&ab_channel=DanceUni)

Starting with leaning on the wall
- whole body straight, just shoulderblades touching
- sitting, back straight, feet further away from the wall
- seeing what changes when I go on the ball of the foot - ball of the foot - stronger counterbalance, more weight

Starting with catching hands in cross position like children and start spinning

Hold doorframe and lean back and explore different positions

Feet sandwich
Leader is enclosing F right foot. All feet are touching, cross hands and slowly move backward and lean. Hands are in the center, above the feet. Straight body. Straight legs.  When exiting, leader is stepping back while he is in the center and then bringing follower back to balance and then he can let go.
## Enter techniques


## Finish techniques

# Classes/Lui and Larrisa headmovement Masterclass.md

---
teacher:
  - "[[Lui and Larrisa]]"
---


> Stages of zouk dancer
> - He fels in love and wants to dance all the time
> - Drilling technique only and forgetting about everything else


## How can you understand headmovements?
There are only two headmovements
1. Spine circumduction (circular movement) - bala
2. body rotation

I do spine circumduction, stop it on the side, start rotating body - it's tilted turn


roasted chicken is the combination of 1. and 2. in opposite direction in the same speed

half of head and twice as much body - side to side chicoque (zarÃ¡Å¾ka)


### Pure heademovements
only 1. or 2. alone
only 1. - balao
only 2. - tilted turns

### Mixing but in the same ratio
toale (same direction)
roasted chicken (different direction)

### Uneven compound headmovements
Mixing differet directions and different ratios


> We can stop headmovement in any point BUT in the beginning the safest is to end up in the sides or down. Back is the most vulnerable position


Then we can add the movement of our legs.
We can do it with 
- moving in the straight line (linear displacement)
- follower is going around leader
	- same direction of body rotation
	- opposite direction of body rotation


For example tilted turns 
- turning follower on the spot
- leading her in the straight line (traveling turn)
- leading her going round me but in the opposite direction of her turn
- leading her in the same direction of the rotation


## Follower technique

### Turning on the place
- using only external rotation of my foot that is in the direction of the rotation
	- it turns in the direction I want to rotate to

### Turning while having some displacement 
They use some ballet technique called shane?

Legs keep the same distance and we just keep turning (kruÅ¾Ã­tko)

The more displacement I have, the further apart follower has her legs
 > Boomerang has big displacement so it's small distance

### Turning around partner
Going to the same direction as the turn
- I have to turn more than just half so I can rotate around partner

Going to the opposite direction 
- easier because F can make steps less than half turn

**How to not get dizzy**
You will get dizzy in the beginning
Practising to be in those positions without the movement either to be just on spot or also with walking

**Spotting**
Imagining that there is something very interesting in front of you and you don't want to miss it. And then starting to turn. 
Not using my upper body or arms in order to move the head. Very often followers pull the hand together with the hand.

## Leading 

### body rotation
Horizontal rotate of the body axes

### spine circumduction
Imagining spreading butter on frying pan

## Frame
What is frame?
Guide for dealing with forces we are interacting with in the dance. 

Takes in account 
- gravity 
- your body structure
- dance structure

Bases for the communication between two bodies to become more effective and predictable. 

**Like conversation - when someone says some word it limits the possibilities there can be afterwards in the sentence. This is what frame does. **

Like when I reach for something behind me. First I move my arm and then I move my body (if the hand cannot reach ). We move one part and once we reach a limit, we move the other party. 

Frame is here to help us transmit the movement through our body. If it doesn't come to our body then the frame was disconnected somewhere.
- We can practise that by doing push ups on the wall but we are trying ot be very smooth. Either by inclining on the wall and pushing or away from the wall and pulling 

> We can try the same with people on the classes 

### Types  frames
1. Manequine 
	Elbows are little in front of body and sideways also a bit away from body (lateral). Don't put shoulders up (if I want to stop myself from falling in push up I also don't raise my shoulders)
2. Balerrina
   We use this in open positions side by side
	![[Pasted image 20230120191702.webp]]
3. Roof frame
	For turns 
	the limit of the mobility is until the hand is perpendicular and in the line of our shoulders and on the other side when the hand is before our forehead.
	for turns or roasted chicken
	![[Pasted image 20230120191958.png|210]]
	![[Pasted image 20230120191948.png|210]]
4. Frame for tilted turns 
Either on the chest or on the shoulder
Elbow of the follower if relaxed.
Hand of the follower is horizontal


In each one of the frames, the line that is created by connecting the fingers of the leader is paralel to one part of the followers body. If I change the line then the body changes.

In manequine the line is paralel to followers collar bones (line of shoulders)

In balerina it connects with the axes that goes forward from the chest

Roof is paralel to the axes that goes from the followers head up

in the tilted turn frame it is connected to the vertical axes of the body

WHen we are leading tilted turns in the tilted turn frame, the hand should be always on the opposite side of axes as the head
![[Pasted image 20230120192936.webp|210]]
![[Pasted image 20230120193030.webp|300]]
That is why it is very hard to do tilted turns with head down, because the hand should be in the back. 


### How do you break the frame?

- giving crossing information that cannot be followed
- giving information that the body cannot follow in that direction

type:: video;
specification:: zouk video
teacher:: [[Lui and Larrisa]];
location:: online

## [[Basic side step]] 

Starting from transfering weight on the L left then together with transfer on right, lower down in the knee and start long step. 

Beginning with [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]], after we start the side step. Most important is to **prepare the long step (going down) on the last step of previous element**. 

==Exercise==
Doing the side step, sometimes [[Simple turn]] and back to side step, sometimes go out to the basic.
> [!HELP]
>  - Important is to make sure they show the difference (if they want to end or continue the movement)
>  - Catching the F as soon as possible after the turn on the back is crucial

We can do it after every [[Simple turn]], we just need to make sure the preparation is clear and we lower down properly in our knees.
- after [[Boomerang]]
- after finishing [[Soltinho]]

- vyzkouÅ¡et rozdÃ­l mezi kroky Tum Äik Äik a jednÃ­m dlouhÃ½m krokem

> [!definiton] Song
> [[Tami Chynn - All night]]
> [[Lola Jane - Leave you]]

![[Grill Chicken#Grill Chicken zaÄÃ¡teÄnÃ­ci [ 1]]

- navÃ¡zat po [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] (jednou a do rovna)
	- vyzkouet si i toÄit dvakrÃ¡t
	- vÅ¾dy u toho zpomalit
- Zkombinovat s prvnÃ­ ÄÃ¡stÃ­ (dlouhÃ½ krok do strany a potom [[Grill Chicken]])
- zkombinovat s tÃ­m obchÃ¡zenÃ­m, co uÄil L+M, [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] > [[Balloon]] > [[Grill Chicken]]

# Dance adaptibility.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
technique:
  - "[[Following in zouk]]"
  - "[[Leading in zouk]]"
  - "[[Reactive frame]]"
  - "[[Follower inspiring the dance]]"
---
This is very important topic for leaders especially when they want [[Follower inspiring the dance|to be inspired by follower]]. Body of leader is not lead by the follower in that moment, his role is to adapt to her body in a way that feels most compatible and comfortable for both of them.

# Dance chemistry.md

---
type: dance
---


We are not moving while the music plays in background. No - we are dancing on the music! There should always be a way how to feel the music. If a deaf man is watching us, he should understand on what music we dance to, he should see the music  

Show the difference between dancing with attention and without

# Dance communication.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
---

Dancing is like speaking language. Sometimes two people don't speak the same language but they want to try to understand each other. One can learn from the second one. Or they don't have to want to understand each other. **If both people want, they can always understand each other in dance**.  [^1]

# Dance connection.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
  - "[[Dance communication]]"
technique:
  - "[[Dancing in close embrace]]"
---
Dance connection is how two dancers communicate and move together as one in the music.

Connection can be used to transmit power and energy as well as information and signals; some dance forms (and some dancers) primarily emphasize power or signaling, but most are probably a mixture of both. [^1]

# Temporary ideas

## From ChatGPT
**3. Physical Connection: How It Feels**

Iâ€™d ask the dancers to **explore different levels of connection**:

â€¢ **Frame**: The structure between partners.

â€¢ **Tone**: The level of tension or relaxation.

â€¢ **Elasticity**: How connection can stretch or compress like a rubber band.

**4. Connection Beyond Physical Contact**

  

Connection is not just about touching handsâ€”it also happens through:

â€¢ **Visual connection** (eye contact).

â€¢ **Musicality** (responding to the same rhythm).

â€¢ **Energy awareness** (feeling each otherâ€™s presence and intention even at a distance).

# Dance creativity.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
technique:
---

Dance creativity is not about training one movement for hours and then execute it perfectly. I see it more as training some general technique over and over until you can just completely relax our of your head, you can trust your body and "go with the flow". Do what body feels on the music.

# Dance empathy.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
  - "[[Dance connection]]"
---



What to do when we feel someone in a dance doesn't want to go the direction I want?
	- How to feel that someone doesn't want to go the direction that I want to go?
		- How to know which direction I wanna go?
			- Which directions I can go?
				- What is influencing me in chosing the way I dance?

# Dance love languages.md

## Energy 
**What you crave**: Exhilaration and Flow
**Your Pet Peeve**: Not dancing full-out
**Want to be known for**: Embodying the spirit of the dance!
**Worst nightmare**: Not being able to use footwork

#### Energetic Dancer Thoughts:
â€œI love capturing the soul of the dance.â€
â€œIt needs more (Sabor/Energia/Spice/Soul)!â€
â€œThe worst thing is when people just stand on the spot and do nothing. How boring!â€
â€œMy favourite music has a nice, strong beat.â€
â€œI donâ€™t mind sweat at all. It means youâ€™re really dancing!â€

#### Common Trends:
Love rhythmic expression; frequently will mention Sabor, Energia, or Spice (if applicable to the dance) 
Very high energy â€“ can go forever
The flow and expression of using their whole body thrills them
Can be frustrated by being forced to stop and chill
Prefer classes where they get to move a lot, as opposed to long explanations or drills

## Deep Connection 
**What you crave**: Fun!
**Your Pet Peeve**: Partners who wonâ€™t smile with you.
**Want to be known for**: Being the â€œFun, Comfortable Partnerâ€
**Worst nightmare**: Making their partner uncomfortable

#### Playful Dancer Thoughts:
â€œEvery dance party is an opportunity to meet fun, new people.â€
â€œThe worst dancers are the ones that make you feel like you are a bad partner.â€
â€œMy favourite dancers are the ones that make their partners smile.â€
â€œThe biggest compliment Iâ€™ve received is that I turned someoneâ€™s night around.â€
â€œI will only keep dancing as long as it is fun for me.â€

#### Common Trends:
Most likely to get a laugh from their audience or partner
One of the most beginner-friendly types
Often more silly, goofy, or light-hearted than other types
A smile and open body language draws them instantly
Often a more social type of social dancer
Mistakes are easy to laugh off as long as it isnâ€™t making their partner uncomfortable; an unhappy-seeming partner is far more serious
Drawn to fun or interesting moments when watching others dance 

## Challenge
#### What you crave: Perfect Synchronicity
**Your Pet Peeve**: Not prioritizing a good partner connection
**Want to be known for**: Feeling good to dance with
**Worst nightmare**: Being rough or uncomfortable to dance with

#### Deep Connection Dancer Thoughts:
â€œI love partners that make me feel safe and taken care of.â€
â€œI donâ€™t care what I look like as much; I just want to feel good.â€
â€œThe worst thing is a rough or inconsiderate partner.â€
â€œI have trouble trusting a partner that Iâ€™ve had a bad dance with in the past.â€
â€œI find it easier to learn through feeling and closing my eyes than thinking about what to do right.â€

#### Common Trends:
Most likely to have their eyes closed.
More sensitive to â€œroughâ€ dancers
Take connection errors more seriously; can be prone to beating themselves up about not following or leading â€˜well enoughâ€™
Prize feel over look.
Not usually competitive, and often care little for shows.
May prefer dancing with safe, known partners than managing the unknown of a possibly rough new connection.

## Challenge 
**What you crave**: Pushing the Envelope
**Your Pet Peeve**: Not trying new things for fear of failure
**Want to be known for**: Being a great dancer
**Worst nightmare**: Being written off as unable to do something

#### Challenge Dancer Thoughts:
â€œI see so many cool things I want to learn!â€
â€œI hate it when I see a dancer doing cool stuff with other partners, and then they donâ€™t do any of it with me!â€
â€œI want to try that again; this time Iâ€™ll get it!â€
â€œI have a list of concrete dance goals I want to achieve, including one-footed turns, splits, and a really cool dip I saw this one time.â€
â€œI get frustrated if I just canâ€™t seem to make something work.â€

#### Common Trends:
Most likely to be in a Lifts and Tricks class
Love complex patterns, and spend a lot of time breaking them down
More likely to work on body conditioning to â€˜unlockâ€™ more potential
Often drawn to competitions, shows, and lifts
Goal-oriented and driven (â€œI want to do that!â€)
Sometimes prone to taking mistakes too seriously, but willing to work to overcome them
Most likely to be bored by a limited repertoire


## Expression

**What you crave**: Musicality and Expression
**Your Pet Peeve**: Dancing the same way, regardless of music.
**Want to be known for:** Musicality and interpretation
**Worst nightmare:** Songs where they canâ€™t find the rhythm

#### Expression Dancer Thoughts:
â€œI love this song! There are so many great opportunities for musicality!â€
â€œThe worst thing is a bad DJ or an undanceable song.â€
â€œIâ€™m just not feeling this music.â€
â€œI wish I could get my body to do all the cool things I think about doing to this song.â€
â€œI love to listen and think about what I can do to different songs at home.â€


#### Common Trends:
Being on time is very important (After all, how can you interpret a song if you arenâ€™t on time?)
Likely to be very attached to what music is played, and follow specific DJs or musical tastes.
Might use â€œbadâ€ music or DJs as their break time.
More likely than average to decline a dance because they donâ€™t like the song.
Often can visualize or think about what they want to do to a specific song â€“ even if theyâ€™re not able to physically do it (yet)

## Creativity.
**What you crave**: New, creative ways of dancing
**Your Pet Peeve:** Only doing what you learned in class
**Want to be known for:** Their originality and creativity
**Worst nightmare:** Being forced to dance within a box

#### Creative Dancer Thoughts:
â€œDance is all about exploring possibilities!â€
â€œI donâ€™t want to be told I canâ€™t or shouldnâ€™t do things.â€
â€œI find really structured classes difficult; I prefer feeling or creativity classes.â€
â€œThereâ€™s no such thing as a mistake.â€
â€œLate night is the best! You can do whatever you want with no judgment.â€


#### Common Trends:
Most likely to be the one rolling on the floor
Capable of leaving the music for the sake of exploring a possibility
Very rarely consider something a â€œmistakeâ€
Can be frustrated by too much structure or too many rules
Usually attracted to unconventional dancers, styling, or music
Not usually competitive in their dance; itâ€™s about their journey



https://danceplace.com/grapevine/the-love-languages-of-dance/
[[Danceplace.com]]

# Dance Teaching pedagogy.md

---
type: dance
---
## Connected notes 
```dataview
LIST
WHERE type = "dance" AND contains(up,this.file.link)
SORT file.name DESC 
```
## Dance teaching pedagogy
As a dance teacher it is very important to know the reasoning behind the movements, to be able to tell students - this is danced like this because of that. But someone else can tell you something different. In [[Zouk]] there are so many approaches and styles and preferences. 

There is also a [[movement intellect]] which states how fast they can make their body to do something they have in their head or what they see. It is not so important if they understand only with their mind.  

Teachers should be open to say everything to anyone. You are not there to comfort them, you are there to help (for example if someone stinks or is not behaving socially acceptable).

Students are babies, we cannot feed the babies with hamburger (all technique with some elements). How much can babies digest? When the baby becomes teenagers you can change the way you talk to them. [^2]
# Wording
- Never say "relax". Especially in connection with the word "have to". It's impossible to feel relaxing. 
- *Try to not think* is also not working. Instead using the expression *put your attention on...*. Not thinking is a state of deep relaxation which happens very late in a dance journey. Especially if we have some exercise it is not possible to not think. 
# Teaching in dance community

Everything you teach you have to make them feel. 

What is different on teaching in community versus a congress? [^1]
- just a small percentage of people are coming because of a dance. Most of the reasons are different like:
	- get social contact
	- get physical contact
	- having something in common with your partner
	- trying something new/exotic
	- having some body movement in their life

Important aspects of a teacher [^1]
- **quality** (dance technique, competence)
- **social aspect, relationship to people**
- **padagogy**
	- feeling for the level of people we are teaching - giving them what they need and exact amount of information, we are not here to present everything we know at once
	- people come here to have fun and learn, having fun also help them to keep the attention span  

### Teaching beginners
- even when we are showing something to them, we are trying to limit our body, so the movement looks more like theirs (that way they will be focused on the most important parts)
- sometimes we can show them a taste of something very advanced (to keep motivation)
- using simple language so they can understand it better

## Recapping the last lessons
- We can give some responsibility to the students - they can show us or at least tell us something we did last time. If we take all the responsibility from them, they will get used to it and not remember so much [^2]


# Reference
[^1]: [[Teachers meeting on StolÃ¡rna]]
[^2]: [[2023-06 Bremen Val and Vanessa teachers course]]


---

# Dancing in close embrace.md

---
aliases:
  - BlÃ­zkÃ© drÅ¾enÃ­
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Dance connection]]"
  - "[[Dance communication]]"
  - "[[Intimity in dance]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Sliding touch]]"
---

> [!NOTE] Leading to close embrace should always be an invitation!


## Close embrace beginners
- First just make them to try how it is to dance in close embrace. Change partners a lot. Then ask for whom was any experience uncomfortable.
- Talk about how to get to and out of the close embrace
 *In any point during a day we can feel differently and it is very important to be true to ourselves. When someone doesn't wan to get closer to you it doesn't have to be caused by you (eventhough it can and always try to smell nice). It can be just their state of body, how their day is or anything else.*
- L try to invite their partners into close embrace, F are choosing, how close they wanna go (see also [[Social Dance Handbook#Consent]])

## Leading into close embrace
Easiest figures where we can get to close embrace (most comfortable is when leader is adjusting his position)
- [[Basic step]] when follower is going front, leader shortens his steps
- Standing on spot

**Make sure that:** 
- you are standing in between each other feet (every feet has its own lane)
- your body is a turned a little bit to the left - so your tools are facing away from the follower
- you are standing straight and not hunched over or bent
## Non-verbal communication of close embrace
### How does leader know that follower wants to get close?
- she is using [[Sliding touch]] when getting closer
- he feels like she wants to hug him
### How can follower let leader know she doesn't want to get close?
From softest to the most obvious. 
1. Changing her steps so she does not get close (usually smaller steps, more controlled)
2. Activating her frame more than usual
3. Placing her hands in front of leaders shoulders so she can push back - only if they feel stronger pull from the leader

If non of these work - then be verbal or stop the dance.

> [!warning] Be careful
> If it should be working, follower has to relax again once the position is gone (once she is in the position she wishes to be in) to let leader know that this is what she wanted.


## Figury vhodnÃ© na close embrace
[[Lateral mirror]]
[[PiÃ£o]]

# Ecstatic dance.md

Recommendation of DJs from Mira Rosa (Australia)
I highly recommend checking out my DJ friends (from my home town, Byron Bay), Ben Templestep, Becca Dakini, and Hamilton Barnett

# Ecstatic DJs
[DJ Arun Ji](https://www.mixcloud.com/arunecstatic/) (Spain)
[DJ Toltech](https://soundcloud.com/toltech1/shadow-10) (shadow dance that I attended on [[2023-09 Bali Zouk embodiment retreat and traveling|Bali]])
[DJ Jobbi Tao](https://soundcloud.com/jobbitao/jobbi-tao-sacred-gathering) (hrÃ¡l jednou na [[Ecstatic dance Brno]])

# Stages of Ecstatic dance
### Arrival: gentle. awakening. graceful. flowy. innocent. stirring.

Arrival tracks welcome the community to the space and the dance floor. They help the dancers feel present, safe, and grounded.  Arrival tracks set the container and create a space to warm up the body and become comfortable in the space. (The tracks often begin as ambient and move into the downtempo realm.)

### Buildup: driving. insistent. throbbing. thrusting. playful. intensifying. rising.
Buildup tracks get the energy moving. The beats are driving and percussive. They help the dancers develop dynamic tension. (Typically, they are mid-tempo.) This stage is when we are starting to build up a sweat and get moving. 

### Peak: wild. surging. chaotic. orgasmic. soaring.
Peak tracks are for catharsis and climax. The beats are assertive, and the bass drops are powerful. (Typically they are high tempo.) Now the dancer has begun to lose themselves in the dance and surrender to the process. 

### Cruise: steady. deep. unwavering.
Cruise tracks are played between peaks, giving the dancers a chance to get recharged. They are the antidote for beat fatigue. They arenâ€™t moving the energy up or down. (They are typically high tempo with temperate beats.)

### Landing: airy. lyrical. angelic. nostalgic. flitting.
These tracks carry the dancers down from the final peak into the heart. This is a period where the body can play freely with a range of style of music â€“  having spent a lot of energy energy and become very comfortable in a space of movement. 

### Integration: peaceful. still. drifting. fulfilled.
Integration tracks are played at the end of the journey to hold the â€œbeingnessâ€ after all the dancing â€œdoingnessâ€. They differ from Arrival tracks in that they feel more emotional, reflective, and resolving. (They are chill and ambient.)

# Elements/Balloon.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - headmovement
Portuguese: BalÃ£o, Volta ao Mundo
Czech: BalÃ³n
---
## Beginners
- sÃ³lo technika 
- F dÄ›lajÃ­ headmovement, L zapojÃ­ rÃ¡m, ale nevedou, snaÅ¾Ã­ se jen pÅ™izpÅ¯sobovat jejÃ­mu pohybu
- vysvÄ›tlit, jak funguje rÃ¡m v headmovementu

### Going from Balloon on the spot to [[Basic step]]
We start on the left side (from L perspective), the head is going down on 7 (little preparation) and 8 up. In this way we can go 1 back to basic. [^1]

### Headmovement in [[Basic step]]
- first starting only steps on a rhytm on the spot
- doing headmovment on a spot (with keeping the rhytm)
- going to the [[Basic step]] but keeping the head only on 1 left side and 5 right side
- trying to connect it

## What to remember

We are controlling the shoulder movement, not the head!
If we try to control the head, the movement will be too big and too sharp.

type: dance element

# Elements/Basic side step.md

---
Czech: ZÃ¡kladnÃ­ krok do boku
type: dance element
specification:
Portuguese: BÃ¡sico para o Lado
---
We start by doing it all solo facing the mirror
1) long side step and chick chick to the feet
2) we imagine that our head is fixed on the rope to the ceiling so it cannot move so much as the body. The body is the end of the pendulum. We try to send the hips to the movement
4) we try to add the step back just straight
5) we turn the hips and do the step futher (just extending the leg back with turned hips)

We try the same thing only facing eachother in couple without holding hands.
Then the leaders offer frame, but not lead anything yet.
*Try to have the same feeling as when you were not thinking about leading it. Just connect your frame a bit more (give it a bit more tension). You make the F move by moving yourself!*

Starting from transfering weight on the L left then together with transfer on right, lower down in the knee and start long step. 

Beginning with [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]], after we start the side step. Most important is to **prepare the long step on the last step of previous element**. 

==Exercise==
Doing the side step, sometimes [[Simple turn]] and back to side step, sometimes go out to the basic.
> [!HELP]
>  - Important is to make sure they show the difference (if they want to end or continue the movement)
>  - Catching the F as soon as possible after the turn on the back is crucial


We can do it after every [[Simple turn]], we just need to make sure the preparation is clear and we lower down properly in our knees.

# Elements/Basic step.md

---
Portuguese: Passo basico
specification:
type: dance element
---
## History

 We are starting with left backward because it is easier for followers. L knows what he is leading and when, but F have no idea. So we want the easier for then.  It's like when are driving the car, for the driver it's always eaiser to prepare and expect the turns compared to the passenger. [^1]

## Basic step ZaÄÃ¡teÄnÃ­ci
### novÃ½ pÅ™Ã­stup [[2023-11-04]]
Na hudbu (can atills)
- rozejÃ­t se do prostoru na tempo, kterÃ© slyÅ¡Ã­, libovolnÃ½ smÄ›r
- stÅ™Ã­dat chÅ¯zÃ­ vpÅ™ed a chÅ¯zÃ­ vzad
- otoÄit se na jednu stranu, udÄ›lat zÃ¡klad ale poÅ™Ã¡d v tum rytmu
- zmÄ›nit rytmizaci na tum Äik Äik 

### StarÃ©  %% fold %% 
CelÃ© na hudbu
- nejdÅ™Ã­v pÅ™enÃ¡Å¡enÃ­ vÃ¡hy na mÃ­stÄ› na hlavnÃ­ doby
- pÅ™emÃ­stit nohy nejdÅ™Ã­v zepÅ™edu dozadu (vystÅ™Ã­dat nohy) a potom do boku
- zvÄ›tÅ¡it krok a nohu, ze kterÃ© jdu tak zvednout a pÅ™inoÅ¾it 
- PÅ™idat Äik Äik do boku
- uÄit na zaÄÃ¡tku bez pÅ™eÅ¡lapÅ¯ (spÃ­Å¡ k noze) - pozdÄ›ji to udÄ›lÃ¡ spÃ­Å¡ zouk, protoÅ¾e budou automaticky trochu pÅ™echÃ¡zet

- nejdÅ™Ã­ve jÃ­t vÅ¡ichni podle nÃ¡s (nesoustÅ™edit se tolik na vedenÃ­) a potom teprve zavÃ©st nÄ›jakÃ© vedenÃ­

## Basic step three-step preparation

Can be connected with [[Front Wave#From Basic step]]

### Rotational preparation for [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]]
In the third step L has to rotate with his body
After that the [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] first two steps are almost on the spot

# Elements/Catch and release.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
---
[[2025-04-19]] na [[2025-04 Castle of Miracles]] jsem zjistil, Å¾e to je [[Gostosinho]]

## Catch and release basic
1) We train only 
   L are going two steps back and hugging F with left hand, releasing the right hand
2) Focusing on making the spring with our legs, lowering in our knees, being more soft
3) Trying to release our partner by coming back to front leg and turning our chest to neutral (don't add any extra energy)
4) show the steps of turn to followers
5) show work of hands to followers
6) show leaders how to change their hand on back of F to get back to basic

## Catch and release + [[Grill Chicken]]

# Elements/Chest movement.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - bodymovement
---

- [[Tiki Taki (shoulders hip change)]]

## Chest movement beginners
- start solo side to side and front to back (open and close chest)
> Help - Exercise with sitting on the floor 
- then trying square (front left back right)
- then trying circle

In couple 
- first just from side to side and front to back
- trying to switch from synchro side movement to asynchro
- from there going to square >circle

## Circles with the chest

# Elements/Drunken step.md

# Elements/Elastico.md

---
English: Elastic
type: dance element
specification:
---
We can connect it with beginning of [[Soltinho]]

## Stop and go
- mention the "safe zone" on the rib cage of follower
- accepting the follower in our frame like heavy ball ([[Frame elasticity and flexibility]])
- L cannot go too far and they need to rotate their step and chest towards partner

## Elastico hook with follower turn
- L is going straight, hooks his hand over F body and turn her on the way back
- It is connection of [[Elastico]] and [[Catch and release]]

## Elastico going around the partner
L are hollding the left hand the whole time
F are trying to go just straign like in basic step and "fill in" the hand of the leader
- we can go either back to open position or to close position and continue with [[Basic step]]
### Leader turning back + Soltinho
In front position leader is not turning back to facing follower but turning back to follower while going under arm. It is important that he doesn't go too far, otherwise he rips his arm off. Finishing with [[Soltinho]]
### Elastico going around partner to [[Shadow position]]
- L is trying to make the second step behind F's right leg, so we don't kick each other
- We can count Tum-Äik-nic, to wait the right amount of time

#### [[Shadow position#Drunken step in Shadow position|Drunken step in Shadow position]]

### NavÃ¡zÃ¡nÃ­ na [[Soltinho]]
- pÅ™i druhÃ© fÃ¡zi obchÃ¡zenÃ­ zÅ¯stane leader otoÄenÃ½ zÃ¡dy k partnerce, podvleÄe se pod svojÃ­ rukou a vede jÃ­ soltinho

## Elastico with [[Onda]]

# Elements/Front Wave.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - bodymovement
---
Pohyb dozadu ve vlnÄ› - jak skokan o tyÄi, kterÃ½ pÅ™eskakuje zÃ¡dy [^1]

PÅ™i vlnÃ¡ch dopÅ™edu pomÃ¡hÃ¡ pÅ™edstava plavÃ¡nÃ­ prsou nebo zapÃ­nÃ¡nÃ­ svetru [^1]

## Legs
When we go forward, we are going on a straight (not locked) leg, when we go back, the back leg relaxes. When we go front, the feeling is like the leg is lifting us up. 

We are trying to not get front knee futher than our foot.

---


We can see it as different stages of one move. When shoulders are going to the stage 1, head is already in stage 2. And they are chasing each other.
*([[Evelyn Magyari]])*

> We can also explain it more geometrically - set up a line before the body, first head goes there, then chest, then hips 


## Bodywave in movement
### From [[Basic step]]
L is starting to lead the wave a little bit before the second step (we can say to the beginner that on the second step), otherwise there is a small preparation with closing the chest beforehand. 
- L is waiting in the second step with chest up and doing third step together with F, letting her finish the wave. He has to make the space a bit larger with his frame (because his body is not finishing the wave)
**Steps:**
Forward, to the leg, forward
### From [[Viradinha]]
The timing for the leader is the same. We have to be careful to
- start leading the wave only when the F is facing us with her chest


# Reference
[^1]: [[Teachers meeting on StolÃ¡rna]]

# Elements/Lateral mirror.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
---
## Lateral mirror

> [!NOTE] We can dance it both in close embrace or on a distance.

- the same beginning as [[Viradinha]] but in the third step L is turning back towards the direction of next step
- Followers - don't forget to make second step longer (more side) - like in lateral
- having some space between L and F (for one more person), having more circular frame. What helps:
	-  facing each other with our chest (hips are going to the direction of our movement)
	- also we can avoid the boob touch on the side
	- leaders are doing a little bit shorter step than the size they are leading, so they always stay more in the middle

### In close embrace (vkroÄenÃ½)
Steps for leader:
1. L: Straight back 
2. Turn chest right, placing the R foot between followers feet (delayed step)
3. L: still turning to get back into the same position as follower (otherwise leader stays more in diagonal position)
4. R: straight back 
5. L: can be placed next to F right foot (doesn't have to be in between her feet)
6. R: turning to get in the same position with follower

# Variants %% fold %% 
## Only leader turning


---

# Elements/OhraÌdka.md

---
Czech: OhrÃ¡dka
type: dance element
specification:
---
## Basic ohrÃ¡dka
- Holding in neutral position and then "add" a bit of tension by L pulling the hands a bit further from each other
- He starts and leads the movement just by moving his own body
- when we finish, we can hold for both hands and turn for L left (under arm simple turn) or we can use the principal of body rotation for turning with L right hand

## PÅ™idÃ¡nÃ­ 4 slow krokÅ¯


## What can cause uncomfortable feeling for follower
- Leader is going too far away (is not in contact with his body to her shoulder in the end of one pulse)
- Leader is going shorter steps than he leads to follower (thus shortening his frame for follower)
- His left hand can be too low, so instead of shoulder area it is going more on shoulder blades

# Elements/Palm wave.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - bodymovement
Czech: Palma
---

IdeÃ¡lnÃ­ pÃ­sniÄka 
DJ Kakah - Never be the same
## Explanation Palm
Imagine like someone attaches a string to your lowest rib and pulls it towards the ceiling. The rest of the body is quite relaxed.

We can imagine our body like separate parts
- head
- shoulders
- rib cage

Each of the parts will get in the finish line (line above our standing leg) in a different time. First it will be our rib cage, then shoulder and then the head. 
- In the [[Snake wave]] it is the opposite

---
Portuguese: PiÃ£o
English: Spinning top
type: dance element
specification:
principle:
  - "[[Turns in dance]]"
technique:
  - "[[VkroÄenÃ½, opoÅ¾dÄ›nÃ½ druhÃ½ krok]]"
---
## Teaching PiÃ£o
V pozici, kdy mÃ¡me oba dva pravou nohu jako centrum dÄ›lÃ¡me kolobÄ›Å¾ku. 

Upravit, aby nepÅ™enÃ¡Å¡eli tolik vÃ¡hu na vnÄ›jÅ¡Ã­ nohu.

Upravit, aby vnÄ›jÅ¡Ã­ nohou chodili vÃ­c po smÄ›ru toÄenÃ­ dopÅ™edu kolem partnera. 


PÅ™echod - musÃ­me udÄ›lat jeden tum Äik Äik na mÃ­stÄ› a pak zaÄÃ­t toÄit (zastavit lineÃ¡rnÃ­ pohyb).
- toÄenÃ­ doprava je pÅ™irozenÄ›jÅ¡Ã­ 
- mÃ¡me jako centrum L pravÃ¡ noha, F taky pravÃ¡
- druhÃ¡ noha kolobÄ›Å¾kuje
	- nepÅ™enÃ¡Å¡et vÃ¡hu na vnÄ›jÅ¡Ã­ nohu moc (stejnÄ› jako na kolobÄ›Å¾ce), jen se odrazit a jÃ­t zpÄ›t do stÅ™edu, tÄ›lou celou dobu zÅ¯stÃ¡vÃ¡ co nejvÃ­c nad stÅ™ednÃ­ nohou
- ideÃ¡lnÃ­ je dÄ›lat sudÃ½ poÄet krokÅ¯ (6, 12), nebo-li sudÃ½ poÄet taktÅ¯ 

kdyÅ¾ se toÄÃ­me do leva, tak se zmÄ›nÃ­ stÅ™ed -  centrum L levÃ¡ a F pravÃ¡
### ProcviÄovÃ¡nÃ­ 
- leader se pustÃ­ a partnerky se snaÅ¾Ã­ drÅ¾et kontakt pÅ™evÃ¡Å¾nÄ› tÃ­m, Å¾e noha ve stÅ™edu se nikam nehÃ½be

## Popis krokovÃ¡nÃ­ od [[Michal ChromÄÃ¡k]]
Popisu kroky lambady z frente tras. 
1) prava noha leadera centrem toceni (napr Pablo) (pocit vic jako zabalim levou, vkrocim pravou do partnerky)
	- 1 vpred 
	- 2 vzad (na puvodnim miste) 
	- 3 diagonalne vlevo vzad 
	- 5 lehce vzad vuci puvodnimu mistu, ale s tim, ze tu nohu nechavam partnerce v ceste, aby vznikl kontakt stehny. Velikost kroku 3 urcuje, jak moc vzad jde krok 5 
	- 6 vpred (jakoby kolem partnerky se snazit jit - zabalovat) 
	- 7 na puvodnim miste kroku 5 
2) stahuju pravou nohu do vecka k leve 
	- 1 vpred 
	- 2 vzad (na puvodnim miste) 
	- 3 diagonalne vlevo vzad 
	- 5 stahnu paty k sobe do vecka 
	- 6 stranou, ale porad s umyslem za partnerku 
	- 7 paty k sobe do vecka 
3) vicemene paralelni postaveni 
	- 1 vpred 
	- 2 vzad (na puvodnim miste) 
	- 3 diagonalne vlevo vzad 
	- 5 vzad vuci puvodnimu mistu, kontakt stehny nevznika. 
	- 6 vpred (jakoby kolem partnerky se snazit jit - zabalovat) 
	- 7 klidne muze cestovat vic do prostoru (nedavam nikdy nohy k sobe a nemam kontakt stehny)

# Variations

## Reverse returning to leader 
Seen [[2026-01-05]] on [[2026-01 Organic Flow Marathon Warsaw]] on [[Manu]]

Using the rotation of the Piao, releasing follower into an outside turn with left hand on 4 beats but directly pulling arm back towards the center of the circle and continuing with Piao again.

# Elements/Snake wave.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - bodymovement
---
## Explanation Snake

We can imagine our body like separate parts
- head
- shoulders
- rib cage

Each of the parts will get in the finish line (line above our standing leg) in a different time. First it will be our head, then shoulder and then the rib cage. 
- In the [[Palm wave]] it is the opposite

### Leading
Leaders are trying to make the movement of the follower a bit bigger by continuing the movement of their body to their frame - elastically.

If we want to lead mainly by our body, we have to tilt it a lot (without tilting the head together with it) and then transfer our weight almost fully to the other leg with the movement. 

We cannot lead [[Balloon]] directly from snake, first we have to go to [[Palm wave]] (to passive headmovement).


---

# Elements/Tilted turn.md

---
type: dance element
specification:
  - headmovement
English:
Portuguese:
principle:
  - "[[Turns in dance]]"
technique:
  - "[[Turning on spot]]"
---
Followers have to learn to not listen their survival skill - always look where you are falling. In tilted turns and headmovements in general, the head is going in the opposite direction of "the fall". This is what makes it so hard to adapt the movement to the body. [^1]

### MoÅ¾nosti ukonÄenÃ­ tilted turns pro followerku:

ğŸŸ¢ V momentÄ›, kdy partnerka dÄ›lÃ¡ boÄnÃ­ krok, tak L vkroÄÃ­ do prostoru mezi jejÃ­mi nohami

# Excercises/Dance directions.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - creativity
created:
---

## Exercise - Dance directions


# Exercise - Dance directions
## One directional dance

**Task**: You need to get from one side of the dance hall to the other

Song: [[Faylasuf - Romance]]

First tell them the task, let them try, then show them how we would do it.

1) you have three 8 counts
2) you can do only specific figures

	a) 1 basic (there and back or continue), open to lunch + turn, viragina
	b) 1 basic, open to lateral + 1 lateral, 1 in and out + turn
	c) 2 basic, lunch + three turns

>Adjust based on the size of the space

## Unusual shapes

One couple will dance and the rest will create obstacles, the couple need to shape his dance to fill the space, obstacles will move a little bit and will react in small movement on the couple

Can be done in several groups


---

# Excercises/Discovering comfort in your body in couple.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - creativity
  - musicality
created:
---

## Exercise - Discovering comfort in your body in couple

## Exercise - Discovering comfort in your body in couple

**Song:** [[Ed Sheeran - I see fire (instrumental)]]

play whole song, so they can explore more options

### 1) Exploring the options
they need to express it with different parts of the body, express is as they feel
choose a posture that is comfortable for you (hug, or a bit further away), let the F choose!

- head + shoulders (headmovement)
- chest ((chest movement) - no hips or head
- hips
- steps

Switch roles

First ask them, what options they found and if follower helped them to discover something new, then show them new options

First we show them one movement, then they repeat it, then we let them practice part song just one part of body

### 2) Being aware of the options
show them options with each bodypart
*ledaers, if you don't know the movement, ask the follower, maybe she knows it and she can help you in that*

- head
	stopping of headmovement, "rolling" in the back, movement only with shoulder or with head in chicoque
- chest
	stopping, or circle, or small waves, palma (jen hrudnÃ­k)
- hips
	swaying, circles, "wave" to the side, small wave

>Talk about impulse versus linear leading

==If there is time==
- steps
	transfer weight, not completely, stop movement, return movement, slow down, speed up, go lower

### 3) Using the music
We gonna play one loop of the song all the time on repeat and they have to find a "sequence" from all parts of the body that will fit to the music. 

*Try to analyse your movement and remember how you do it, try to always do it the same way, or at least the same movements. Analyzing yourself is big portion of becoming musical and creative*

1) L are trying to duplicate their sequence with several F
2) L are trying to describe to the F, what are they dancing
3) F have to describe them what they are doing (they can use their body)
4) F have to try to dance the sequence without L leading
5) **BONUS** - F are trying to dance the same sequence with the next L. So he can feel, how the L before him is dancing and get inspired.

### 4) Positioning

Try to dance the same sequence or at least the same feeling and timing just in different positions.

- hug with different hand on top
- L is going from both sides (first one then another)
- L from behind
- lateral position
~~~~


---

# Excercises/Dynamics and timing.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[William Texiera]]"
tags:
  - musicality
  - creativity
  - dynamics
  - communication-in-dance
---
Teacher: [[William Texiera]]
Event: [[2022-09 Zouktime! Croatia]]

#### Solo
Everybody alone had to make some pose on 1 and 5 and switch it every time. On other counts they were perfectly still. 

Then instead of stop they will continue the movement in slow mo . So make the contrast on the right count but continue in soft movement. 

#### with partner
The same. First sharp and without continuing the movement . Then with reverb (continuing the movement )
Trying to avoid doing only headmovements (that is our usual tool for expressing the dynamics)

>** idea **
Follower can lead her idea on 1 and follower can do it on 5 (they did it based on my impulse)

Speaking about the communication in a dance. We don't think about it much about leader and follower. We are two people listening and feeling the same music. We cannot talk both at the same time. 

The follower leads the pose and then there is important to communicate! Maybe the follower doesn't have any more creativity for the reverb etc. So just feel yourself together and create the dance 

Based on when we prepare (chicoquote) then it looks different dynamics. If we prepare on 8, then it will have softer feeling , if we prepare half beat before 1, it gets more dynamic


---

# Excercises/Exercise - What feels comfortable for your body.md

## Exercise - What feels comfortable for your body

**Everytime go one type of exercise on all the songs**

Songs: 
[[Birdi - Skinny love]]
[[Sariel Orenda, DeviRa, Mose - Azul]]
[[Pabllo Vittar - K.O.]]
[[Sage the Gemini - Watchachacha]]

### Solo
1) with closed yes on the spot
	*explore the movement of your body, what feels comfortable for you and what you feel in the music*
2) you can play only with your upper half of body (from hips up)
3) only the bottom part of your body (including hips)
4) only steps
5) combine everything, choose which song tells us what

### Couples
Trying to do the same, switching also roles. *Don't think about leading so much. Relax your frame and let anything happen. Be aware of your partner. *


# Reference
type::dance
specification:: exercise
teacher:: [[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]
tags:: self expression

Dancing together, trying to use this idea of balls. There is no mistake.

# Excercises/Exploring and expressing contrast in music.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - musicality
created:
---
## 
## Exploring and expressing contrast in music

Exercise - Exploring and expressing contrast in music

> [!Example] Song 
> Momofuku

1. Play the song, let them dance freely, get to know the song
2. Go through the song together, say what are the differences in each part
3. Limit the dance and trying to express the contrast in the limit (after they dance each option, show them our example)
	1. Staying in close embrace, no body shapes, no headmovements, only STEPS
	2. Staying in close embrace with body shapes
	3. Open embrace with simple elements
	4. Only headmovement (for advanced)
	5. Only body shapes (chest + hips)
4. Combine it in their own way

## Version 2

sadasdas

# Excercises/Expressing the melody of songs.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - musicality
created:
---
## Exercise - Expressing the melody

> [!example] Song
> [[Arianna Grande - 7 Rings]]


1. express only "bells" in the background, ignore rhythm and voice. Express body movement to the side. then add some smooth movement (various waves) and add bells to it. Contrast!
2. the melody is often repeated, has some structure (see phrase)
3. Count, then clap to it. then sometimes try to turn off the music (just the volume) so that they continue dancing
4. Then connect more regular bells (we express both). by moving for each time we express the bells regularly and with some contrast (perhaps using another part of the body) we express what was before
5. **for the more advanced** - we can make a continuous slow movement with the chest and express the emphasis with a faster movement (but everything fluid)


> [!Warning] Challenge
> We can try walking together with the chest movement

### Extra Challenge
> [!example] Song
> [[Emmit Fenn - Painting Greys]]
1. Show them how it would look if I try to express every single note (very noisy)
2. Show them how powerfull it is just to try to express the beginning and the end of a melody pattern
   > Try to relax from the idea of expressing every note, sometimes it is impossible and you wouldn't have a nice dance, but there are always another options, if you catch the beginning and the end (mostly the end!) of every melodical phrase, it will look amazingly and feel also
3. Let them try

## Expressing the melody of songs


---

# Excercises/Expressing the mood and energy of song (on a sequence).md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
created: 2021-01-01
tags:
  - musicality
  - creativity
elements:
  - "[[Gorilla movement]]"
---
## Exercise - Expressing the mood and energy of song
In song we can follow several layers of a song
1) tempo
2) rhytm
3) melody, frequencies, singing
4) mood

Last two points are the ones that make the biggest difference in expression of advanced dancers versus intermediate. Also because they are the hardest and least regular of them. 

> [!example] Songs
> [[Lola Jane - Leave you]] or Delacey - Dream It Possible
> [[Pabllo Vittar - K.O.]]  or Duda_Beat - Deixa_Eu_Te_Amar
> MC Lipi - Praiou or DJ Kakah - Delilah or MC Rodolfinho - Velho Ditado or Mc 2K, Igor Sales & Malharo - Cheiro de Rosas

Play a minute from each son and let them dance.
> What is the difference between those songs? What differences you made in your dance to express each of them?

1. Teach them one phrase
2. Let them try on normal music
3. Show them a different feeling of a song, what can they change in general
4. Try one phrase with changes on the song
5. Teach next phrase

### Sequence that we gonna use

#### Basic version
**Feeling**: Classical

> [!example] Songs
> [[DJ KRON - Baby]]
> Anselmo_Ralph - Virou_Amo
1. Phrase
   [[Basic step]] > [[Lateral]] > Getting close together from the left side >twice  [[Front Wave]] - [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] - [[Basic step]]

2. Phrase
[[Basic step]] > [[PÅ™evedenÃ­]] > [[Basic step]] > 3x [[Front Wave]] > UsazenÃ­

3. Phrase
Open [[Lateral]] > pÅ™ekrok > twist twist > [[Front Wave]] > [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]]

#### Slow lyrical song
**Feeling**: Slow motion, smooth

> [!example] Songs
> [[Lola Jane - Leave you]]

##### Changes in the choreo
1. Phrase
On the left side when we get closer from lateral make 2x slower [[Front Wave]]

2. Phrase
One small wave and second one slooooooow

3. Phrase

Slow transfer of weight instead of twist

#### Playful song
**Feeling**: Work more with your knees and changing hight of your dance, work more with your hips - release them
> [!example] Songs
> [[Pabllo Vittar - K.O.]]
> [[Pabllo Vittar - Amor de Que]]
1. Phrase

In close position make a swing with hips together

2. Phrase

Instead of waves make [[Chest movement#Circles with the chest|Chest circles]]

3. Phrase

Make the twist twice and a little funky

#### RnB/ deep
**Feeling**: Try to be grounded, don't lift our level of shoulders at all
> [!example] Songs
> Mc Lipi - Praiou
> Mc Rudolfinho - Velho Ditado
1. Phrase
Different rhytmicallity of steps on lateral
In close position 2x [[Gorilla movement]]

2. Phrase
Instead of wave do side diagonal steps R L RR L R > [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]]

3. Phrase
Twist, sharp wave (chest hip) > [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]]


---

# Excercises/Get inspired by follower.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - communication-in-dance
  - social-dance
  - creativity
created:
topic:
  - "[[Follower inspiring the dance]]"
  - "[[Dance adaptibility]]"
---
## Exercise - Get inspired

**Discussion**
*How does your follower inspire you in a dance?
How and in which ways do you take inspiration from your follower?*

### Understanding the hug
> [!example] Songs
> Groundfold - the final chapter
> Justice Der - Don't kill my vibe
> Aquillo - So close to magic
> SYML - Mr Sandman

Leaders close their eyes and girls change. Every time girl comes she chooses how close she wants the leader to be. And guys have to try to feel it and respect it.

Show followers a way how to let the guy know if they are not comfortable with the distance
### Get inspired
> [!example] Songs: 
> [[Birdi - Skinny love]]
> [[Sariel Orenda - Suenos de Libertad]]
> [[Pabllo Vittar - K.O.]]
> [[Sage the Gemini - Watchachacha]]

We put different music every 30 s, they are just in a hug and followers are trying to move their body (no steps) on how they feel the music. Then the guys are trying to incorporate this in the dance (on the spot)

*Leaders, you try to look like you are leading. So from the outside I don't want to see any difference.*

### Work with the inspiration
First the F suggest some moves and mood of the dance (as before), then the L tries to overtake the dance (leading), but with the same feeling and elements as the F started

### Create a different dance
Take inspiration from F - start to lead - create a dance with this mood and style, try to have your dance but incorporate what you felt and "heard" from the F

### Practice
On some random music they can try to do the same only without any instruction on timing. 
*Find some time in the music where you try to give the F some space for expression, she/he may or may not take it. If it happens, take it as an inspiration and continue from there.*


---

# Excercises/Inspiration circle.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
  - "[[KlÃ¡rka]]"
tags:
  - creativity
  - self-expression
---
## Exercise - Inspiration circle
Everybody stays in a circle. We choose a body part (for example hip movement). Then we play some song or a loop melody and go around the circle. Everyone has to come up with a new version of movement (new version can be also slowing down or making it bigger but there has to be some visible contrast). Teacher is always going in the middle of the circle and trying to explain shortly, how to do this movement. 

>Can be done solo and in couples


## Exercise - Inspiration circle n.2  [^1]
*Every group is going to show us their favorite movement in the end, so you have to choose one. Then when you are ready, you can sit down. Don't forget to try to explain what you do to others, especially when you see someone struggling or not knowing how to lead/follow it.*

- first make a big circle (with us in the center) and show them how it works - tell 3-4 random couples to show us and we all repeat
- divide them into groups from 5-10 people (depending on the size of the group)
- tell each group to choose the most original movement, when all people from the group show one
- when they finish, they sit on a ground (so we know the whole group is finished)
- every group is showing their favorite movement to everyone 

Let them dance one song when they connect some of the movements together with the steps.



[^1]: [[2023-04 Spring Zouktime! Brno]]


---

## Keeping the flow during changing partner

Can be used also in any lesson with changing during a training on a song

---
Leaders are dancing and when I say change, followers are staying int he last movement leader was leading. Leaders are going to another Follower (also with some basic step), trying to adjust to new F steps and continue the dance.

## Leaders leading only with their body
Good position to exercise at: 
Leader is in position of [[OhrÃ¡dka]] (arms wrapped around partner, perpendicular), tries to lead for follower either step forward or back only with torsion of his body.

*We can do before:* 
Leaders on the spot, F staying in open lateral position. L is leading her steps around her in circle only with rotation of his body. 

Leader staying on the spot, with feet together. Leading only with their chest rotation.

# Excercises/Leading linear vs impulsive.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[Anderson and Brenda]]"
tags:
  - leading-and-following
  - technique
created:
---
They were teaching it on [[2022-11 Zouk family retreat, Mexico]]
## Leading linear vs impulsive

1) One leg in front of other, Bones are stacked, but joints are free, upper body is also free. Partner is pushing F from 0 to 10 gradually and the F is trying to transfer it to the ground. She just receives the energy and sends it to ground, not pushing to the partner (no contra resistence). She is trying to have the posture a little bit leaned forward just by positioning the pelvis a bit back.  (More important is the posture than where I have the weight - I can have weight fully on my one leg, but if I have wrong posture it will not work)
2) Trying to give F certain amount of energy so she/he moves only certain amounts of steps (they go into pair of couples. One couple always show with hand to the other couple, how many steps he wants to lead. If he succeeded the other side is clapping)
3) Try to connect the same thought to a body movement (so F goes only half of the wave)


---

# Excercises/Music with the same speed but different energy.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - musicality
created:
---
## Music with the same speed but different energy

KaÅ¾dou pÃ­sniÄku projet celou a aÅ¾ pak jÃ­t na dalÅ¡Ã­, nezapomenout ukÃ¡zat naÅ¡i verzi!		

With every song there are the same phases
1. Play the song, let them listen. Talk about:
	1. What feeling do they have?
	2. What instrument or element of the song is giving them the feeling
	3. How tould they express this energy in their body (with their partner)?
2. Let them dance on the song
3. Show them how we would dance on it
4. Describe, what does it do for our body

> [!example] Songs
> [[DJ KRON - Catch and Release]]
> [[Branko - Made of Gold]]
> [[LANY - I.L.Y.S.B.]]
> [[Lemaitre - Higher]]

> [!Question]
> Which song was the fastest? 
> *They are all the same speed, only the instruments and elements of the music is giving you a different feeling.*

Song, where the energy is changing a lot and rapidly
Amigo - Lost
