# Excercises/Playing with basics.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - creativity
created:
---
## Playing with basics
Always do it like this
- show what we gonna do
- do it all together
- show them tools they can play with

> [!example] Songs
> Gloria_Groove_feat - IZA_-YOYO
> Wixard XO - Nuh Behaviour
> Alina Baraz - Lavender and Velvet
> Alina Baraz & Galimatias - Maybe

### basic step
- we start [[Basic step]] and there try to figure out way how to play with this. Show them what is it made of - just steps. We can use them, to repeat them, back forth..
- do steps just forward and backwards and then show them that they can rotate it
- play one song only with basics

- show them that they can either go just back, just forward or make locks (just transition of weight)
- after the transition we can make wave (show them how to play with it after - you can do some isolations on the spot, ladies can also try to inspire)

### open lateral

First try the movements solo
- we go to open position and in there we try to play, 
	- hip gorilla movement,
	- sway fro side to side,
	- waves or a palm


### lateral

- we stop on the left side, we try to move shoulders up and down and then we try side wave

---
- let's try to play now, so I don't want to see any patterns, but use the elements we learned and with the help of music use them in a playfull way
- followers can sometimes also try to suggest some movement in still positions, guys try to be perceptive


---

# Excercises/Playing with phrasing with theory.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - musicality
  - theory
created:
---
## Playing with phrasing with theory

![[1691767279113.jpg]]
### Rhythm

rytmus

ZaÄÃ­t kreslit, vysvÄ›tlit rytmus, vysvÄ›tlit dÃ©lku tum a Äik, pustit jednu pÃ­sniÄku, aby se na to zamÄ›Å™ili

PokraÄovat s nÃ¡kresem, vysvÄ›tlit frÃ¡zovÃ¡nÃ­, pustit hudbu a snaÅ¾it se to v tom najÃ­t, co se zmÄ›nÃ­ apod

### Phrasing
> [!example] Song
> [[DJ Kakah - Safe place]]

1. Stopping before the phrase ends
   - We will try to stop always before the phrase ends on the last 4 beats (8 eights) ends on 5,6,7,8 and start on 1.
2. Fluent stoping with a wave
   - Now try to be fluent in the break (end the movement softly and use it to transfer the weight), show them normal wave
3. Changing contrast with the phrase
   - Try to focus on the music change, if the energy is going up, start moving, if the energy is oging down, try to do only slow weight transfer with one step
4. Using the fluent stopping but in their dance 
   - try to dance only simple things
   - show them some examples

> [!example] Song
> [[Robin Thicke - Lost without you]]
1. Stop on a melodical change in music, start on the beginning of new phrase
2. Use the melodical change to make some fun element that we gonna show them (for example chest movement) with the rhythmicality of the melodical change
3. Try to use the same logic but with any element they choose
   - first they try and then we show them some examples
   - as a challenge they can always try to do something different
4. Leaders just stop and let the followers do anything and then they start
5. **Challenge** for F: Every time they have to create something different
   > very good in the end of some lesson because it brings lot of laughs


---

# Excercises/Playing with Phrasing.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - musicality
  - creativity
created:
---
## Playing with Phrasing

> [!example] Song
> [[Robin Thicke - Lost without you]]

1. Let them find a repeating musical pattern in the music (8th Tum Äik Äik)
2. Stopping on the pattern and only transfering weight
3. Try to stop with reverb (controlling your movement before the stop and then going as slow as possible)
4. Show them some examples in different positions

> [!example] Song
> [[Can Atila - Mara Despina]]

1. Stop every time she stops singing (later it is only instruments) - third Tum Äik Äik, with slowing down on two bars

> [!example] Song
> [[Feverkin - Overthought]]

1. We can try to express first start and finish of the melodical pattern
2. Try to express every tone
3. You can try to change between 1 abÅ„d 2

# Excercises/Social dancing, dancing on small space.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
tags:
  - social-dance
created:
topic:
  - "[[Dancing in crowded space]]"
---
## Social dancing, dancing on small space

We stand in very small space (that is very important). Couples create a circle. There are several exercises we can try.

1) Roda (like in tango). We always try to move forward. L react on a movement of the L before them. 
   >this makes them do simple things and concentrate on the dance as general
2) Dancing on a spot, they can look around and when they get eye contact with another leader, they switch places with each other. 
3) The same thing as before but also with changing places they have to change also partners.
4) It's possible to do the same on the whole dancefloor (but then it is needed to talk about "stealing" partners in a dance)


---

# Excercises/Unusual rhytmicallity.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - exercise
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"

created:

## Taught at %% fold %% 
```dataviewjs
dv.table(["Backlinks"], dv.current().file.inlinks.map(f => [dv.fileLink(f.path)]))
```
## Unusual rhytmicallity

**Song:** [[Ed Sheeran - I see fire (instrumental)]]

Melodic patterns
1_1 / 1_1 2 /3_2 / 4_1 2 / 1 4

First solo then in couples. 
1) clapping or stomping on the beats
2) doing some sharp movement
3) trying to have "reverb" on the movement (moving linear and sharp contrast)

*Try to dance on the song and find the patterns*

show them expressing different notes (most natural will be always 1_1)
REPETITION (the melody often repeats)

[[Can Atila - Mara Despina]]
[[Ashram - Elizabeth]]
[[Woodkid - Brooklyn]]

**Challenge on the end** 

[[Emmit Fenn - Painting Greys]]

# Excercises/Using silence in the dance.md

## Workshop from [[Paloma Alves]] about using silence in a dance on [[2022-11 Zouk family retreat, Mexico]]
Exercise where we walked around with different speed and when she said we started talking (or making sounds) and when she said silencer we tried to stop. She made us to come closer and closer and make it louder and louder and then stop  It was about the tingling sensation in the body. 

Then we tried to use it in a dance - first connecting on distance, trying to transfer weight together, connecting first with chest and then hug slowly. Trying to use the silence. Keeping eye contact from F (sometimes eyes, more often chest). Then we try to use the combination of silence and sound of movement

> Types of contrasts (for example distance, size of movement, tension, speed)


type::dance
specification:: exercise
teacher:: [[Paloma Alves]]
tags:: self expression


---

# Expressing contrast in dance.md

Tools that we can use: 
- bigger/smaller
- lower/higher
- fast/slow
- movement/stillness
- soft/sharp
- close/distant

# Finding limits of your partner.md

One partner is receiving. Lays on the ground, the other person is trying to let him feel the weight of their own body. To lift their legs, move them in very simple movements. Listen to the body of the laying person. Trying to help him by listening his limits. **You can find limits only if you are very soft**. Helping the person to notice - if we feel they hold some muscle tension, ask him if he knows it, that there is a tension. [^1]

Don't see the limits as something limiting you, but expanding your options towards certain direction. Like putting a pipe in the water. [^2]

# Resources
[^1]: [[Anderson and Brenda]] in [[2022-11 Zouk family retreat, Mexico]]
[^2]: [[Mateo Trevisan]] in [[2022-11 Zouk family retreat, Mexico]]


---

# Flow in Zouk.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
technique:
---

[[Flow]] can be accessed in a state of effortlessness. 

Flow can be accessed when we let go and let ourselves be carried away by anything that is coming. [^1]

Flow is created in a state of balance between many aspects 
surrender X discipline
structure X spontanaity

- [[Ashe]] and [[Ellias]]

# Following in zouk.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Principles of leading and following]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Following through the frame]]"
  - "[[Momentum-Based Following]]"
---
Follower should react in a way of [[Relaxed action]]. 

If the follower is [[Non-reactivity|non-reactive]], it helps to create relaxed actions. Sentence, that can help the mind and body can be *I donâ€™t need to move until I feel a clear impulse.*

## Basic rules follower should follow 
1. Respecting her / his own body
2. Respecting the direction of leading 
3. Respecting the size of energy giver to her body by the size of movement

## Relaxed following
1. Follower is standing in relaxed posture (minimal tension needed to be standing in healthy posture)
2. Lead is starting the preparation of movement 
3. The follower begins sensing information through the preparationâ€”tension naturally starts to build as energy accumulates.
4. The follower consciously relaxes to let the information complete its flowâ€”without letting the tension spread into emotional reactivity or the upper body.
5. Leading energy gets so high that it gets easier to move than to stand
6. [[Relaxed action]], the follower moves with clarity, honoring the direction and energy of the lead without adding excess effort. Using the inertia of the energy while keeping her body integrity and activity.

# Frame elasticity and flexibility.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Frame in zouk]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Momentum-Based Following]]"
---
In the full stretch of elastic moment, it should feel like two ropes connected and gently pulled apartâ€”firm, responsive, and ready to move, but never rigid.
If you lock your elbows, then it will feel like two sticks. 

Elastic moment is a combination of maximum distance in your arms together with the size of your step and how far you move your body center between your legs. Your weight in elastic moment should always be at least in the middle, otherwise it will not be comfortable for you and you won't make proper step.

# Frame in zouk.md

---
aliases:
  - taneÄnÃ­ rÃ¡m
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
technique:
  - "[[Frame elasticity and flexibility]]"
---
> [!Definition] Definition
> Frame is not a shape or one particular tension level, it describes the mechanism through which movement information travels from one person to another. 

Most "initiating" information flows from the leader to the follower, but information flows both directions constantly. 

Bracing (or active tension) for our body means protection. It is expecting something that could go wrong, something that could be dangerous. [^2]  ^600607

# Typy rÃ¡mu 
## Na zÃ¡kladÄ› vzdÃ¡lenosti

### VzdÃ¡lenÃ© drÅ¾enÃ­ 
### Basic vzdÃ¡lenost
### BlÃ­zkÃ© drÅ¾enÃ­ ([[Dancing in close embrace]])

## Na zÃ¡kladÄ› pozice kontaktnÃ­ch bodÅ¯
### SymetrickÃ½ 
- ve vzdÃ¡lenÃ©m se drÅ¾Ã­me obÄ›ma rukama 
- ve standardnÃ­m mÃ¡ L obÄ› ruce na zÃ¡dech partnerky, stejnÄ› tak F
- v blÃ­zkÃ©m to stejnÃ© 
### AsymetrickÃ½ 
- ve vzdÃ¡lenÃ©m drÅ¾enÃ­ pouze jedna ruka 
- ve standardnÃ­m levÃ¡ strana L otevÅ™enÃ¡, pravÃ¡ uzavÅ™enÃ¡ 


# Position of Frame %% fold %% 
We want to have our elbows to be wide (wider then the position of hands). hands mostly paralel to the ground. 
If we move our elbows closer to the body (in the "inner circle"), it will mostly make our hands rotate up and distort the impulse. 
If we move our elbows too wide, it will make our shoulders [[Upper back backbend#Shoulder position is important too|internally rotate]] which moves the shoulder blade further away from the spine and reduces the stability of the whole back. Therefore breaking up the connection between the arm and the back. Also it can cause the chest to collapse and feel closed. 

Keeping allows and wrist flexible so they allow the energy to pass through them and work also as some sort of cushion. Keeping a slight tension to avoid collapse of frame. 

Focus on guiding your energy from center rather then from your arms. 





The goal is generally to have the minimum level of tension at any given time to facilitate a smooth flow of information between dancers - which can change depending on the forces and directions involved. However a higher or lower level of tension - while it wouldn't be the most "efficient" generally speaking - could create a different set of movement possibilities than the more efficient frame, so choosing to engage to a greater or lesser degree may have advantages (especially if it's done intentionally for that reason). I always teach minimal necessary tension as default because it's easier to add some tension situationally than to remove some. ([[Zouk nerds podcast]])


---
In turns, shoulders are the part of your body that is determining your balance.[^1]

# Headmovements.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Basic posture in dance]]"
  - "[[Flow in Zouk]]"
  - "[[Frame in zouk]]"
connected_with:
---

## Headmovements
We cannot start headmovement until we learn to walk with each other ([[Xandy Liberato]])[^1]

We don't have to lead the exact size of the movement of the head, because the head is influenced by the shoulders and chest. So always try to make it smaller. 

>try to find some good example on how to make it closer to people

# Holding hands.md

## Basic embrace
### Follower
- trying to read information from leading mainly with left hand on leaders back (or back side of his arm/shoulder)
	- hand is not dead, it is trying to be active and aware all the time
	- arm is resting on leaders frame (not pushing!)
- right hand has the same tension as when we are holding hands with our life partner during walk.
	- it is uncomfortable if the hand is sloping and leader has to hold it with more tension
	- trying to close the hand so it can relax more
#### Don't do
- pushing partner either with left hand towards you or right hand down (or giving it too much tension)
### Leader
- with right hand trying to catch the shoulderblade of our partner
- when we come to the embrace, we are offering our frame to the follower

## Close position 

## Open posture (lateral)
### Follower
- try to use only the first part of your fingers to create tension (closest to the hand)
### Leader
- offering his hands
### Both
- out hands should be lower than our elbows
- the feeling of frame should be like holding a grapefruit under our arm
#### Don't do
- use thumbs for holding!!


type:: dance
specification:: principle
tags:: technique

# How to break a frame in a dance.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Frame in zouk]]"
connected_with:
---
## Basic options for leader to break the frame [^1] 
1) Using the inertia of the body (for example in [[Dance/Elements/Open to the right]]). When it would be too hard to keep the frame in the moment, so instead the frame relaxes. 
2) Changing the angle of the hands
3) Bringing hands into the "empty zone" - the center of the body of the follower

[^1]: [[Lui and Larrisa headmovement Masterclass]]

# Indivky/Individual lesson from Nina.md

---
type: individual lesson
teacher:
  - "[[Nina Darbello]]"
price: 60â‚¬
---
Connecting shoulder blades. Exercise when you do lifts (zvedÃ¡m se za nÄ›jakou tyÄ nahoru) with hands and not letting shoulders getting to your ears. Keeping this feeling.

Matching the energy with your partner, then you don't have to fight in a dance. 

When she has a heavy leader, she adds energy in the shoulder blades.

The changes are showed by tension in body or shoulder blades or steps. Or by breathing in. 
> For beginners, when we want to stop, just try to bring more weight into one step, just break the pattern
> Teaching beginners to not lead all the time, just give the impulses. Is it possible? When and how?

Leaders rotate the elbows up then he cannot put shoulder up. Followers the same. When we are in the close position, follower is just trying to close the frame a little bit to create contact (to not go up with frame everytime she feels the leader do the same)

> Head movements with frame - when we have a line of joints we can be quite relaxed and don't have to connect our shoulder blades so much. But when the impulse is not going through the joints we have to connect the shoulder blades more. 

**my technique**
Try to focus on using shoulder blades for me frame
Giving more energy into tilted turns and normal turns. Focusing on making big circles and pushing into the shoulder of follower (even can have contact on the shoulder). 
In normal turns try to have the hand lower (exercise when we create a house with hands connecting on our center of forehead and then we just use the one hand.)
When I want to finish tilted turn with some head movement or controlled movement, I have to give tension already before the finish, contraction down and then lead the finish. 

Exercise when we tried to dance firstly completely without tension in shoulder blades - then we have to be ready that anything can happen - follower deals only the impulses from body and legs.
Then we tried to have a dance with keeping the tension in shoulder blades all the time (but trying to not connect biceps). Controlling every movement. It was very hard to create a flow, to not be relaxed in relaxed movements.


---

# Indivky/Individual lesson from Vanessa.md

---
type: individual lesson
teacher:
  - "[[Vanessa from Iago]]"
price: 110 â‚¬
---
# [[2024-02-23]]
## General
The whole experience was amazing, I accepted the premise from the beginning - I don't want to mainly improve my technique, but get inspired from her way of dancing. First we had few dances to align a bit more. Then I asked her if she can unleash her creativity more and that I will adapt to her. I really enjoyed which ideas she had and the way she was expressing them. At any time it didn't feel enforced or disconnected, she was suggesting and when she was not suggesting I always felt her connection.
Overall I am very satisfied with the state of my dancing now and what I can create just with little time and opportunity to align together with her. 

## Questions I asked

**What do you say to followers that are bit more shy with low self esteem about her expression in a dance?**
V: First I ask if she wants to express herself in a dance (because some followers may want to just follow).
V: Then I would tell her to go to some solo dance class, to find something that she really likes and makes her body move. Which then she can try to implement in certain movements she knows from zouk. 
V: If she does not want to put so much effort into classes etc, I give her some exercises that she can do in a dance. For example chose one part of a body that she should try to express with. 

## Comments to my dance
When I dance to fast music or very dynamic music, I tend to give less space (which is understandable because there is less space and time). Also tension in my frame gets bigger and it is harder to recognize some dynamics because I don't make such a contrast before starting some change. 
She did not feel I would lead too strong even when we tried to add some more dynamics in the dance.
After tilted turn, if I want to make some change and lead some transition, I should start changing the tension in the frame when F is already on her left leg (I already see her chest), so sooner. (the same was saying [[Individual lesson from Nina]]). Also she was correcting me that if I let the F hand closer to her chest (so she can have a bend frame) it will be easier for her to engage.


---

# Indivky/William Jahn - individual lesson.md

---
type: individual lesson
price: 50 EUR
teacher:
  - "[[OndÅ™ej KrÃ¡l]]"
client:
  - "[[William Jahn]]"
date_start: 2025-04-10
notetoolbar: Individual lessons
---
## 1. Lesson [[2025-04-10]]
Posture
- often times when he is in close embrace, he is leaning back, thus leading first with his upper body and having a bit of falling feeling
Stepping
- when he goes forward, he rotates his feet together with his pelvis and that does not allow him to relax the pelvis and also make a proper step
- often he misses steps (f.e. second step in Viradinha) which disturbs the clarity and comfort. Or when he leads something faster or different timing, he is not syncing his steps with follower so it is not so precise

How I structured the lesson
1. Dancing normally on a song
2. Dance without any body shapes and headmovements 
3. Dance on slow rhythm, stepping all the time, focusing on stepping together with the follower 
4. We were correcting the posture and stepping a little bit 
5. Going just back and forward with attention on his legs, posture and going clearly 
6. Still in a slow rhythm but using also frame and further distance for leading any steps and turns. Focus on the follower steps so you always turn her in the right direction on right leg
7. Dancing regular zouk elements in the slow rhythm
8. Switching from tum Äik Äik to slow rhythm
	Here the problem with clarity was usually slowing down. He slowed down too late and it wasn't clear. I told him to focus on his stepping in the second step and it helped a lot. Then I showed him that it is possible to slow down like this almost anywhere where we change direction.


---

# Intimity in dance.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
up:
  - "[[Intimacy]]"
principle:
  - "[[Dance communication]]"
---
Why are there so many interactions in zouk that are misinterpreted as sexual or that they should lead to something? 
> Maybe one of the main reasons is that we (men especially) used to have so much intimacy in our life and not in many forms. We are used to  [[Intimacy|intimacy]] = [[Sex]], but there are many forms of intimacy. Thanks to dance we are able to feel this intimacy first hand and it can blow our minds. Wow, I have never experienced something like this, this has to be something special and I should pursue it.

I already went so long way in a dancing that I can enjoy only the connection, only the intimacy we share in a dance. And that does not have to be the same intimacy we would share on our way to some relationship or sexuality. And in the same time it can be. 

There was a point in my way where I took every intimate connection as "that could lead somewhere" and also used to [[Clinging on things|cling]] on the person instantly. Creating automatic pressure on the connection which was causing more of disconnection than what I was eager for.


---

# Leading in zouk.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Principles of leading and following]]"
  - "[[Dance adaptibility]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Frame elasticity and flexibility]]"
---

We never try to force as leader. We try to convince. Not by force but by ourselves moving differently with our body (example when he started to move fluently in front of Vanessa and she started moving subconciously)[^1]


- Leader never has to carry the follower

# Momentum-Based Following.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Principles of leading and following]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Frame elasticity and flexibility]]"
  - "[[Following in zouk]]"
---

> [!definition] Definition
> The follower continues a movement trajectory, initiated by the leader, until a **limit**â€”internal or externalâ€”stops, redirects, or transforms that movement.

## Types of limits

| Limit type            | Description                                                  |
| --------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Anatomical (internal) | Follower reaches the physical boundary of her body position. |
| Partner-based         | Follower is stopped by the frame of the leader on her body.  |
| Enviromental          | Spatial constraints, floor, walls, other dancers...          |

**Anatomical limits should always be respected in relation to a healthy, aligned** [[Basic posture in dance|posture]] (i.e. the shoulder shouldn't go out of its position, the body shouldn't lean forward etc.) and to the most relaxed and elastic version of [[Frame in zouk|frame]] in that position.

# Musicality in a dance.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
technique:
  - "[[Musicality layers of a dancer]]"
---


Brenda: Some songs give more attention into how we feel and some into how we move. [^1]

In general it is most often seen as how you decide to move your body (with your partner) to interpret some music. 

1. dancing in the beats
   your dance is expressing everything that is in the music. It is the "obvious" choice
2. dancing on the beats
   looking at the song from above and deciding what you express. You understand the music you hear and your dance is adding something extra to it, not always "visible" in the music. You are expressing the music in your own "words". So you follow and respect the message of the song, but adding something to it. 

You don't want to seperate them, you want to be great at both.

# Rhytmical changes
## Emphasise one

### 1) quick- sloooow
Making the steps before the one all quick and then prolonging the one for twice the time
[Like in this video](https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=817114566851246) at 3:53

# Musicality layers of a dancer.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
connected_with:
  - "[[Musicality in a dance]]"
---


## Layer 1
Being able to follow a tempo of a song with his own steps/movement.

## Layer 2
Being able to follow a timing of a rhythmical pattern (beat) with steps.
## Layer 3
Respecting the phrases of a song with simple dynamic of movement - softer phrases no or little movement, more energetical phrases - movement with steps
## Layer 4

# My dance philosophy.md

---
type: dance
up:
  - "[[0_Dance MOC]]"
specification:
  - personal
---

Dance is a relationship that we create for limited time on the dance floor. As in life it depends how balanced this relationship will be and from which place you want to create it. Also who will talk more, if both of you are listening and co-creating this relationship.


---

# OndrÌŒej + KlaÌrka teaching couple.md

## Bio
KlÃ¡rka and Ondra both developed a profound love for music and dance from an early age. KlÃ¡rka, in particular, found her passion for dancing at a young age, starting with ballet and then exploring various dance styles. Additionally, both of them played musical instruments since childhood. These early experiences formed the basis for their deep emotional connection to the art of dance.

More than 8 years ago, they discovered salsa and bachata, but they soon fell in love with zouk. They were captivated by its beauty and complexity. They focused their development in their hometown dance studio, StolÃ¡rna, led by LudÄ›k and Pavla LuÅ¾nÃ­, and also attended international congresses.

As teachers, they began by organizing workshops on musicality and creativity in Brno, and soon they started teaching internationally in places like Romania and Germany. One of their main goals is to guide local dancers in the right direction and help them understand the essence of dance connection.

Ondra, with his experience as a DJ, shares his passion for music with his students, teaching them how to express themselves and understand the music. KlÃ¡rka, who has explored various dance styles, brings her fresh and inspiring dance style to zouk. They aim to go beyond the traditional knowledge of zouk, teaching not only movements but also different mindsets that supports creativity and enhance social dancing skills.

## Price

# Pricing of individual lessons.md

---
up:
  - "[[Individual Lessons MOC]]"
---

## Prices of other teachers 
[[Gui Prada]] - 150 dollars ([[2025-10-05]])
[[Moni NÄ›niÄkovÃ¡]] - 900 CZK ([[2026-01-03]], informace of [[Katka SedlÃ¡kovÃ¡]])

## Why teaching a couple costs more money
> [[2024-12-18]] jsem uÄil pÃ¡r za 1000 + cenu sÃ¡lu a pÅ™iÅ¡lo mi to jako dobrÃ¡ cena.

**Enhanced learning experience**
- you are essentially getting two lessons in one session as teacher is instructing and correcting both of you 

**balanced progression** 
- teacher is concentrating on the couple to progress in the same speed together, additionally he can give more tips and details to one person which is more comfortable with his body

**Interaction management**
it takes much more energy and presence to balance the interaction and synchronisation between two people

# Principles of leading and following.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance principle
principle:
technique:
  - "[[Following in zouk]]"
  - "[[Leading in zouk]]"
---
> [!example] Example: Leader Carrying vs. Active Following
> Imagine helping a child jump onto a high curb. If you try to lift them without their help, it's heavy and uncoordinated. But if the child bends their knees with you and **uses your upward impulse to jump**, the movement becomes smooth and shared.

WHERE type = "event" AND contains(topic,this.file.link) AND !contains(file.name,"Template") OR type = "dance" AND contains(specification,"dance class") AND contains(topic,this.file.link) AND !contains(file.name,"Template")
SORT file.name DESC

# RnB rhythm in Zouk.md

[[Zouk rhythms]]

## [[Lateral]] in RnB Rhytm

**Options for leaders:**
- Stepping next to the leg
- Crossing second step to the back
- Not doing the second step  (just two slow steps)

## Teaching RnB to beginners
- start solo [[Basic side step]] with cross to the back, first trying only on 1 long step and 3 step next to the feet 
- trying two rhythms - taaa ta ta (1, 2 and half, 3) and ta ta taaaa (1,2,3) - further mentioned as RnB rhythm and inverted RnB
	- shoulder line in the same hight all the time (balancing with knees and ankles)
	- very sharp step on 3rd beat, stop my movement afterwards completely (later there can be a small reverb after the stop)
	- third step very small, trying to stay with body front
- leading a back step to the follower in [[Basic side step]]
	- same principal as [[Viradinha]] but with lower body, we rotate our hips and through our frame F feels it
	- the more sharp step we doy the more clear we have to be in our frame


Trying [[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] in inverted RnB rhythm. Important to connect it together with preparation. 
- after preparation I am turning on the spot with first step. Second step is also almost on the spot 



From teaching with [[Moni NÄ›niÄkovÃ¡]]
Simple sequence: 
[[Dance/Elements/Lunge]] > [[Boomerang Reverse#Clasic Reverse Boomerang]] (in the end they can do side basic step) in RnB rhythm


---

# Setting up boundaries in a dance.md

---
notetoolbar: dance
type: dance
---

## How follower can show boundaries 
From softest to most firm 
1. Adjusting steps 
2. Adding tension in her frame / body 
3. Placing a physical boundary on leaders body (stiffen the frame, put her hand on the chest of the leader when he wants to take her closer)
4. Saying out loud what she feels and what could make it feel better




## ğŸ”— SouvisejÃ­cÃ­ poznÃ¡mky
- [[Boundaries]]


---

# Silence in a dance.md

Music is comprised from moments of sound and absence of sound - silence.

Silence in a dance means having minimum tension in your body your need to be able to communicate with your partner. That tension in your body is also influenced by your calmness of mind.

Silence in a dance and in a couple is not happening when we are distracted and disconnected from our partner. It is the same feeling as when you are falling asleep hugging with your partner in bed.

What thoughts inside of **leader's head** are often causing tension (and getting us out of the [[Present moment|present moment]]):
- I am boring / I have to make some exciting things to entertain my partner
- I am not good enough to express this music
- I am dancing too basic things

What thoughts inside of **follower's head** are often causing tension (and getting us out of the [[Present moment|present moment]]):
- I understand it wrongly and disrupted the dance
- I make too many mistakes
- I am not following precisely
- I am not giving him good enough technique/ I am not good enough for him

# References
[[2024-03 La Primavera PlzeÅˆ#Workshop s Moni NÄ›niÄkovÃ¡ - Ticho v tanci]]
[[2022-11 Zouk family retreat, Mexico#Workshop from Paloma Alves about using silence in a dance]]

# Teaching through experience, not mind (embodied approach) - inner child.md

---
type: dance
up:
  - "[[Dance Teaching pedagogy]]"
---

**Traditional approach:**
The instructor explains â€” the student executes. The process is led by words and correction.
*Put your right foot forward.*

**Embodied approach:**
The instructor creates a _situation_ for discovery. Concepts are named _after_ they are felt.
*Take a step as you walk towards someone you want to hug.*

## Teaching through inner child
Our goal is to try to speak and act towards the **inner child** of our students. To wake up curiosity, playfulness, imitation and the trust that our body knows what to do. 

**Adult mind** operates through logic, instructions, corrections. It thinks that it needs to understand the movement before it can execute it. 

Adult mind often approach dance with:
- performance anxiety (*â€œIâ€™ll do it wrongâ€*),
- overthinking (*â€œAm I on the right count?â€*),
- self-consciousness (*â€œHow do I look?â€*).

Our role as a teacher is to help the adult mind temporarily switch off. 

> The most embodied and natural way to learn is to first let the inner child explore and play â€” discovering what feels good in the body â€” and only then invite the adult mind to give names to what the body has already understood.

|                   | Adult mind      | Inner Child            |
| ----------------- | --------------- | ---------------------- |
| **Learning Path** | Understand â†’ Do | Do â†’ Feel â†’ Understand |

It can be sumed up into two steps: 
1. _Somatic discovery_ â€” body-led exploration creates intuitive understanding.
2. _Cognitive integration_ â€” language and naming consolidate that experience.
## Language of the instructor
- using more methaphors and feeling based approach 
	- *imagine you are moving through a water*
- sensory prompts 
	- *How do you feel in this movement?*
	- *Where in your body you feel the tension?*

**Avoid:**
- technical description of the movement too early before your students experiences it in the body
- too much correction during exploration (can disrupt the flow of exploration)
- evaluation as *right* or *wrong*. You can use wording as *let's try different approach/version now*

# Traditional zouk music.md


It's important to remember that there is no musical genre called "Brazilian Zouk". What really defines "traditional music" is not some specific genre but how the music feels and body responds to it. Typically these are songs with soft, rounded and steady beat that creates the characteristic pulse. That pulse is what guides the body's movement.
[^1]

We can see all the influences of Brazilian zouk development in [[Zouk history]].

[^1]: https://www.instagram.com/p/DQCtGjYkjBD/?img_index=6&igsh=MThkbmJ3cWo4cDJlZQ== Post on traditional zouk music of [[Brazilian Zouk Council]]


---

# Tresillo.md

Tresillo is first part of [[Son Clave]] which is the most common clave pattern in Cuban music (like [[Salsa]]). [^1]



[^1]: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VTe-1lvfL14

# ss

When turning in spot, we often use footwork when we:
1) Move one foot to the direction of the turn
2) Replace the original place of first foot with second foot
![[Pasted image 20240112111003.png|300]]
![[Pasted image 20240112111014.png|310]]

Second option is to use the Paddle footwork (like we are going on a scooter or skateboard) [^1]

[^1]: [[Lui and Larrisa headmovement Masterclass]]

# What creates comfortable headmovement leading.md

---
type: dance
specification:
  - dance technique
principle:
  - "[[Frame in zouk]]"
connected_with:
  - "[[Headmovements]]"
  - "[[Leading in zouk]]"
  - "[[Frame activation]]"
  - "[[Frame elasticity and flexibility]]"
  - "[[Reactive frame]]"
  - "[[Connection of frame and body in leading]]"
up:
  - "[[Headmovements]]"
---

**Using our chest for leading the movement**
The movement of the body should come from the same place as the followers movement, only our head is staying upright. Movement of the body of leader can become smaller and smaller with time as the body learns to adapt to the movement and be more clear. 

**Adaptation ([[Reactive frame]])**
- the way leader is capable of adapting to followers:
	- range of motion 
	- irregularities 
	- tension/softness/relaxation level/tone of muscle
- receiving the body weight of follower with reactive frame instead of fixed

**[[Connection of frame and body in leading]]**
If the leading comes only from the frame it will always feel stiff and less comfortable for the follower. 

**Using legs to create and slow down the movement**
Especially when we receive the follower in the end of movement, it is very important that we use our knees to soften the movement. 

**Grounding**

**Support**

**Clarity of size and direction**

# Zouk history.md

---
up:
  - "[[Zouk]]"
---

## 1. The Origins of Zouk Music and Its Meaning
People from French caribbean islands wanted to create some music of their own, that is why zouk was created. Zouk was inspired by many other dance styles like kompa, carimbo and others. 

The term "Zouk" originates from Antillean French Creole and translates to "night long party." This term was popularized in the Caribbean islands of Guadeloupe and Martinique, where Zouk music first emerged. In the late 1970s, the band Kassavâ€™ played a crucial role in defining Zouk as a music genre, blending Caribbean rhythms with contemporary sounds. Their song "Zouk-la sÃ© sÃ¨l mÃ©dikaman nou ni" ("Zouk is the only medicine we have") helped Zouk gain widespread recognition across the world.

Then came Zouk Love and Zouk BÃ©ton. 

Semba, Kuduro, Taraxxo, Kizomba came from French people that heard the french carribean islands zouk music and started to mix it into new styles. 

Ghetto zouk is coming from Cape Verde (didnt understand this word properly)
## 2. The Birth of [[Lambada]]
Before Brazilian Zouk, there was Lambadaâ€”a dance style that originated in Brazil in the 1980s. Lambada was heavily influenced by folk dances such as CarimbÃ³ and Maxixe, as well as foreign styles like ForrÃ³, Merengue, and Salsa. It was characterized by fast, intricate footwork, circular movements, and the distinctive close embrace of partners.

Lambada music, popularized by bands such as Kaoma, quickly spread internationally, particularly with their hit song "Lambada" in 1989. However, as the Lambada music trend faded in the 1990s, dancers sought alternative music genres to continue dancing in a similar style.

The name came from the word *gitahada*  (slap on the guitar) - when the DJs in clubs wanted to wake up the crowd. Lambada in portuguese means also *slap*.

Lambada became very popular with the band Kaoma which tried to make lambada the hit of carnival and that also helped the lambada to spread worldvide. In Kaoma there were only two brazilian people. Kaoma was playing mainly in Paris. Then the music was brought again in Brazil.
## 3. The Transition from Lambada to Brazilian Zouk
Lambada died a little bit with a movie called "Forbidden dance" that introduced lambada as a dirty dance that you should never dance. 

As Lambada music became scarce, Brazilian dancers began incorporating slower and more melodic Zouk music from the Caribbean into their dance. This shift began in the mid-1990s in Rio de Janeiro, particularly at the Ilha dos Pescadores nightclub. At the forefront of this transition were dancers and instructors such as Adilio Porto and Renata PeÃ§anha, who adapted Lambada to fit the rhythms and structure of Zouk music.

This adaptation required modifications to the dance itself. While Lambada was traditionally danced with fast, sharp movements, Brazilian Zouk adopted smoother, more flowing transitions. The steps evolved from the Lambada basic step into movements incorporating elements of Bolero, Samba de Gafieira, and Tango, leading to the unique style we now recognize as Brazilian Zouk.

Brazilians also started to dance on music that was played on radios and from there new styles got created.
## 4. The Development of Brazilian Zouk Styles
As Brazilian Zouk gained popularity, various styles emerged, each bringing a unique approach to the dance:

- **Traditional Zouk (Rio-style Zouk):** Maintains the original elements of Lambada with some modifications to accommodate Zouk music. It can be danced both linearly and in circular patterns.
- **Lamba Zouk (Porto Seguro Style):** A high-energy variant that retains more of the original Lambada elements, characterized by fast-paced footwork and head movements.
- **Neo Zouk:** Created by Mafie Zouker, this style focuses on contemporary musical influences, often danced to electronic and chill-out music.
- **Soulzouk:** Developed by China (Xina), this style emphasizes biomechanics and body awareness, allowing for more organic partner connection.
- **Zouk Flow:** Introduced by Arknjo, this style incorporates elements of hip-hop and urban dance, focusing on natural movement and rhythm.
- **RnB Zouk:** From Renato Veronezi 
- **Contemporary zouk:** Xandy and Evelyn, Pasty and Josta influenced a lot 

Also thanks to Mafie and other DJs, people started dancing longer together, because he had longer songs and was mixing a lot. 
## 5. Brazilian Zoukâ€™s Global Expansion
By the early 2000s, Brazilian Zouk had spread beyond Brazil, with dance communities forming across Europe, North America, and Asia. This was driven by traveling instructors, international dance congresses, and the internet, which allowed dancers to share videos and teaching materials globally.

In 2006, a significant meeting was held at the Minas Zouk Congress in Belo Horizonte to unify the global community under a common name. After much debate, the term "Brazilian Zouk" was chosen to distinguish it from the traditional Zouk dance of the Caribbean.

## 6. The Role of the Brazilian Zouk Dance Council
In 2014, the **Brazilian Zouk Dance Council (BZDC)** was established by prominent figures such as Larissa Thayane and Kadu Pires. The council aimed to support and promote Brazilian Zouk worldwide, setting competition standards, ranking systems, and fostering the growth of the dance community.

# Notes unstructured %% fold %% 
In Antillean French Creole, Zouk means party! 


Brazilian Zouk Rio de Janeiro Style is a couple dance that is coming from mix of Lambada / Bolero / Samba de gafieira / Tango / salsa / hip hop and others inspiration ....  
The name Brazilian Zouk is used to distinguish the dance from the Caribbean Zouk dance, which is historically related to, but very different. The 2 dominant lines inside of Brazilian Zouk are Zouk (Zouk Rio Style) and LambaZouk ( Porto Seguro Style ) and we have anothers ways to dance our Zouk ( Zouk Rio Style ) with different styles let me try to explain you.

Zouk (Zouk Rio Style )

Jaime aroxa brought lambada to Rio de janeiro in 1988 the sucess of this dance was great .  
We had so many places to dance , we have so many people at old ( Roxy Roller da Lagoa) the biggest dance place of lambada in Rio de janeiro , was amazing place with more the 2000 people dancing lambada .  
We had 3 special groups of dancers in this time , jaime aroxa students , Carlinhos de Jesus students and a favela .... yes Favela was one small group of dancers that called Lamba 7 ( Aipim / Mandioca / Plinio / Pinguim / Felipe / Buiu / Adilio Porto) my name in my group was captain Bolero because they already saw that i was not dance only lambada , hahahhahah , i was dance already one mix of lambada and ballroom dance Brazilian , of course that my lessons of ballrom dance with jaime arouxa already start to change my dance .  
After the big sucess of lambada in Rio de janeiro , where we had alot of lambada places amd many many dancers, start to be difficult to dance lambada because so many things happend and so many people stop the only place that we had was Ilha dos Pescadores .

Zouk Rio style was first developed in Ilha Dos Pescadores in Rio de Janeiro around the mid 90's when Lambada songs stopped being composed and we start to use gipsy king songs and Zouk music .Adilio and Renata was teachers at Jaime aroxa dance school and dancers of Bolero , Samba , salsa , Tango , Ballet and Lambada , so after jaime aroxa stop the teach Lambada , they start to teach this amazing mix of dances and they start to call the Zouk and the first lessons of this new dance was developed and first taught by Adilio Porto andÂ Renata PeÃ§anha FullÂ in Brazil's most famous dance school Jaime ArÃ´xa. They danced to the slower music of the Caribbean Zouk , Gypsy kings and some others sonhs similar to hip hops and rnb songs .this making it easier to learn and vary steps, moves, patterns and combinations. The characteristic steps that were created are the basic step going front and back (from Samba de Gafieira), the opening and lateral step (from Bolero), elastic and bonus (also called boomerang in Europe). Viradinha , Raul ,Soltinho and others steps.  
Since adding lots of new steps and changing the characteristics from Lambada, a new name was given to this dance, another things that made Adilio and Renata change the names was because the real dancers of lambada was not more accept that adilio and renata call this dance of lambada , because was already another dance and as well because the music that was playing at ilha was Zouk , alot of dancers start to call the dance the zouk .the name give was originally 'Zouk Love', later just called 'Zouk'. Today we are calling the Brazilian Zouk for not have problems with the zouk dance of France, Martinica and Guadalupe has changed the name has been given to the dance that was first tought by Adilio and Renata in the beginning of the 90's, which is now didactically used all over the world.

Unlike salsa, which is led with the hands, Brazilian zouk is led by more parts of the body. Sometimes, in a basic sideways movement, it is the hips that move first, followed by the rest of the body, and this is part of what makes the dance so sensual. However, in various moves the dance partners are also connected by eye contact, legs, arms, shoulders, head, etc.

When practicing zouk in dance classes, teachers generally warn women to be very careful with their backs and necks, as two of the most distinctive and commented-on movements are the cambrÃ© (arching backwards to a greater or lesser degree, sometimes even below the waist) and the specific 'hair movements' or ' head movements' for the woman. If not done properly this could lead to injury.Â   
Zouk Rio Style got really strong outside of Brasil more the 50 countries and almost 200 cities are dancing ....

[[Lambazouk]]
LambaZouk, also called the Porto Seguro-style, is often thought of as the evolution of original Lambada, although in its current iteration it has divulged far from original Lambada. This dance is characterized by high energy (energia) and feel good attitude (alegria). Although it is a fast and energetic dance, it flows smoothly and the moves are continuous and rhythmic, and dancers follow circular (and to a lesser extent slot-style) movements as they relate to each other. One way in which the present LambaZouk differs from the original Kaoma-like Lambada style, is that they have removed wiggling shoulder movements (also sometimes seen in Cuban-style salsa). Instead the shoulders are kept fixed while the hips move (swing) to create a sensual effect. A number of movements have been added to the modern version of this dance mainly created by Didi Santos of Brazil.

LambaZouk is characterized by the following movements:

Head movements (CabeÃ§a - head moves in the same direction as shoulder; Boneca - Head moves in the reverse direction as shoulder for half measure (1-2-3))  
(Hair) whip movement (Chicote)  
Back arch/dip (Cambre)  
The original Porto Seguro style is also unique in the way steps are performed to music (in this sense it is closer to Lambada). Here, the steps are performed with equal emphasis (same amount of travel) on strong beat and the two beats that follow (including the pause after the strong beat). This is done specifically to facilitate musicality by matching sharp movements (Chicote and Cambre) with the strong beat. When danced this way dancers fluently incorporate sharp movements to accentuate strong beat without stopping the dance (pausing to catch up). Even though this timing is popular in LambaZouk it is by no means exclusive. Many LambaZouk dancers also dance by taking longer step (or turning the follower) on the dominant beat (like Traditional Zouk). It is also a common practice to switch between the two timings within the same song (by doing multiple contra-tempo turns for the follower). For comparison on timing, Traditional Zouk emphasizes strong beat by having dancers take a long step on the strong beat. In LambaZouk style (as explained earlier) a popular way is to step equally (length-wise) on strong beat and following two beats. This creates continuous movements.

LambaZouk is danced to rhythmic, up-tempo music (tempo is generally fast or medium, rarely slow), whereas Traditional Zouk is more suitable for slow tempo music (often with long pauses). Kizomba music is very popular in LambaZouk owing to its rhythm and pace. Because the music faster, and head movements are more sophisticated and done more often, dancing LambaZouk requires better technique and timing in order to perform head movements without injuries.

LambaZouk is mainly danced in Porto Seguro, SÃ£o Paulo, Belo Horizonte, Argentina, Spain, UK, Israel, the west coast of the US, Japan & recently also in Malaysia. LambaZouk is also evolving to include more modern movements. It is also not uncommon (lately) for dancers to switch fluently between these dancing styles during a single Zouk music song.

â˜† Zouk (Rio Zouk Style ) with different styles â˜†  
As mentioned above, several new styles can nowadays be distinguished. The dance is changing and developing all the time, adding and changing techniques of dancing, leading and following, but keeping the frame and pattern of Traditional Zouk (Zouk Rio Style). New musics are also part of this development, leading to various new movements and interpretation of the music. Some styles are mentioned here, which are danced now in many countries:

Neozouk - : it's a of Brazilian zouk, that aims to show different trends in zouk , created by Mafie Zouker ( Student by Adilio & Renata), where the gentleman uses his lady as inspiration to conduct his dance exploring every articulation, to define each movement, the difference between conduct and respond is in the direction in which the movement occurs, because there is times when the lady induces the gentleman to a different path , continuing the movement.

Soulzouk - was developed in 2005 byÂ China SoulzoukÂ ( Student by Adilio & Renata) a teacher from Rio, Brazil. Soulzouk, (also called "zouk freestyle" by the inventor) differs according to China from Brazilian zouk in the way it connects with the music.

The Soulzouk dance style is, not only based on the pace, but also on the melody of the song. It can be danced to zouk music, but it is also taught to be danced with a variety of other musical genres, like rap or RnB, that don't have the zouk beat.

We have others new styles from amazing dancers likeÂ Renato Veronezi FullÂ , Bruno Galhardo , Jefferson Dadinho ,Â Xandy LiberatoÂ that i will try to get more informations from than to write here.

---


[[Lambada]] was first known in Europe and then it came to Rio de Janeiro. That is where it first changed into zouk love in 1996, took inspiration from [[samba de gafiera]], [[tango argentino]], soltinha (basic folklore dance in Brazil) then the bigger changes came from names like Adilio Porto, [[Mafie Zouker]] or [[Xandy Liberato]]. 
Information by *[[Alex Carvalho]]*


In the 80â€™s, Lambada was very popular in Brazil and quickly gained worldwide notoriety through its music, especially because of the popularity of the band Kaoma, Beto Barbosa, among others, and different styles of music such as Samba-Reggae, Caribbean Zouk, Flamenco music, mainly Gipsy Kings, among others. TV shows, films and DJâ€™s also helped promote the dance and the music.

[[Lambada]] was a dance that dominated most nightclubs in Brazil, especially in Porto Seguro, SÃ£o Paulo, Belo Horizonte and Rio de Janeiro.

[[Lambada]]'s popularity began to decline in the 90â€™s, and the remaining lovers began to use primarily Zouk Caribbean music to continue dancing Lambada. During this period people naturally began to call the dance French Lambada, because of the music being sung in French Creole. Following that the community began to call the dance [[Zouk]].

As a result of the Zouk music having different characteristics from [[Lambada]], soon the [[Lambada]] dance began to adapt to the [[Zouk]] music. the dance was naturally modified, acquiring different characteristics in various states of Brazil and some places in the world, creating interpretations and different styles of Zouk. 

The French Antillean Creole term zouk was first used on the islands of Guadeloupe and Martinique to refer to nightlong dance parties.
In 1979 Guadeloupean sound technician and bass player Pierre-Edouard DÃ©cimus and guitarist Jacob Desvarieux formed Kassavâ€™, the group that integrated the diverse styles of mizik zouk, injected the mixture with a contemporary urban, studio-produced sound, and marketed the new music as zouk. With the overwhelming commercial success in 1984 of the groupâ€™s song â€œZouk-la sÃ© sÃ¨l mÃ©dikaman nou niâ€ (â€œZouk Is the Only Medicine We Haveâ€), zouk was firmly established as a new and viable Caribbean dance music genre.


There was a time when several names were created making it difficult for the community to promote Zouk dance. Several meetings and debates took place and the community understood that the name Zouk was inappropriate because the dance and music already existed in the Caribbean. 

Around 2006, there was an important meeting at the Minas Zouk Congress (currently BH Zouk Congress) in Belo Horizonte, in order to define the official name of the dance and unite the community. The Brazilian Zouk name was decided by majority of votes. Until 2012, there were many meetings, lectures during dance congresses around the world to bring awareness and popularity to Brazilian Zouk name.

In 2014 the Brazilian Zouk Dance Council was founded by Larissa Thayane and Kadu Pires. The Council serves, supports, and promotes all aspects of Brazilian Zouk. We encourage the growth of this great dance throughout the world. The Council is supported by its board of directors â€“ Gilson Damasco, Renata PeÃ§anha, Alex de Carvalho, Kadu Pires, Larissa Thayane, Jaime Aroxa, Rafael Oliveira, Philip Miha, Rodrigo Delano, and Freddy Marinho.

---
"History of Neo, Flow and Soul. [^2]

Around the 2000s, after the transition between Lambada and Brazilian Zouk, three styles emerged, more urban and with contemporary influences in Rio de Janeiro, aimed at the experience on the dance floor: Neo, Flow and Soul.

Flow is a set of techniques developed by Arknjo. In its genesis, it was

inspired by fluidity, rhythm, and the state of Flow. It aims to prioritize the quality of contact techniques

in motion to achieve a more comfortable, intuitive, and organic dance. Arknjo is also a music producer and event producer responsible for several memorable parties in Rio de Janeiro keeping the scene alive since the 2000s.

Neo, created by Mafie Zouker, is a trend focused on stylish movements and always looking for new influences and new movements. In addition to Mafie being a pioneer in the creation of remixes for Zouk and ended up creating a new musical aspect when he mixed elements of Zouk Rnb, electronic music and chill out.

China was on the scene since Lambada and in the transition he adapted his style of dancing with shorter and more tanned movements and in the perception that his way of dancing was different, Soul Zouk emerged.

Together, China, Arknjo and Mafie were of great importance in the construction of contemporary/modern Zouk in Brazil and around the world."


----

A question was posed regarding the origins of our dance. Where? When? Who?
History is important. But great dances are not created overnight by one person, or in one place at one time. These are dynamic, creative processes. In the case of Lambada - and subsequently Brazilian Zouk- we have to look at its creation as being developed from several different dances and movements. Africa gave us many of these movements. One has only to watch the movements of sacred orixÃ¡ dances, as well as popular African dances such as Lundu, Carimbo and Maxixe to recognize the major dance influences that led to the later crystallization of the early forms of Lambada - including hip and head movements. Forro also influenced the development of Lambada and - according to at least one Salvadoran scholar - so did polka. The point is that before Lambada music arrived, all these aforementioned dances were flourishing especially in parts of Brazil that had populations with African heritage. So the Lambada music and these dances traveled around the country from northern parts of Brazil like Belem and became melded together in certain centers - notably in Porto Seguro where there were spaces for the development of the dance such as the Lambada school in the church square in Arraial dâ€™Ajuda and at the Boca da Barra in Porto Centro. It was in Porto Seguro that the dance began to take real form, with a recognizable style and rules and competitions. Of course, it was danced in the bordellos of Porto, which meant that the dance had a notoriety right from the beginning. But this â€˜forbiddenâ€™ quality of the dance (which was also present in its predecessors Lundu and Maxixe)  only served to make it more popular. People came to Porto Seguro from many other parts of Brazil to watch and dance Lambada at the famous cabana â€˜Boca da Barraâ€™. Eventually Lambada music and dance gained worldwide popularity when the group â€˜Kaomaâ€™ was formed to promote it and became enormously successful. I really want to stress that although it may have seemed to Rio or SÃ£o Paulo dancers that Lambada lost its popularity - but in Porto Seguro it NEVER DID. Bahianos have been dancing this beautiful dance in its purest contemporary form since the beginning - often facing enormous opposition and judgement which exists even today. Dance spaces were burned down, lambadeiros were judged to be immoral and ostracized. Fortunately, the Porto Seguro government has recently declared Lambada to be an important cultural entity. This has only taken forty years!
But if a dance gains sweeping popularity as Lambada did, it will always have to rely on the continued creation of new music. For various reasons known best to the commercial music industry, after the demise of Kaoma Lambada music began to be replaced by different rhythms. Radio stations lost interest and moved on to the next craze. There were still many people who still wanted to dance Lambada but students in Rio and SÃ£o Paulo became hungry for new styles and new music. Dance teachers in many places were losing money. So it is no surprise that Lambada metamorphosized into a more contemporary form and was repackaged as â€˜Zoukâ€™ - which happened to be the name of Caribbean music from Martinique and Guadalupe that had a similar rhythm to Lambada. They renamed classic Lambada steps - Lambadaâ€™s â€˜Basic 6â€™ became â€˜Lateralâ€™. â€˜Diagonal Twistâ€™ became â€˜Bonusâ€™ etc etc. But it was still actually ... LAMBADA. People with backgrounds in other dances - Renata Pecanha for example - added touches that brought a Contemporary Dance flavor to Lambada. It started to be danced slower, in a linear rather than circular pattern, more upright and with less movement in the hips, all of which was easier for people with European backgrounds. The more complex and difficult moves of Lambada such as Boneca - which was created by Master Didi and his then partner Rebecca Lang and subsequently developed by Master Braz and others in the Boca da Barra - were left behind. The fascinating â€˜Desprezadaâ€™ was itself â€˜ignoredâ€™! Why? Probably because it was considered too difficult for the masses and therefore not marketable. And the â€˜Diagonaleâ€™ - a basic and essential element of Lambada that creates stability, beauty and an excellent preparation for turns - was also lost.
In reality, no one can be blamed for trying to repackage a beautiful dance, even though it involved a certain amount of â€˜dumbing downâ€™. Even the lack of acknowledgement that Brazilian Zouk was, at its foundation, Lambada, was understandable. Less forgivable, in my view, was - and is - the failure to acknowledge the essential African nature of the danceâ€™s foundations and the African origin of its rhythms. Such a shocking omission may have been based in blatant racism.
Of course, some repackaging attempts simply involved renaming Lambada: â€˜LambaZoukâ€™, â€˜Zouk-Lambadaâ€™ and many more. And there was a group of Caribbean dancers who had serious objections to â€˜Zoukâ€™ - the first new name for Lambada. People in Martinique and Guadalupe for example already enjoyed a local dance called â€˜Zoukâ€™ that was nothing like Lambada. So enter a consortium of individuals who chose the name â€˜Brazilian Zoukâ€™ (incidentally that occurred without consultation with the Bahian Masters who had created the original form of the dance).
To come full circle, I want to reiterate that all dances are dynamic; they will continue to develop and change. The developers of Brazilian Zouk were more privileged in terms of education and had better marketing skills than most Bahian lambadeiros so little wonder purer Lambada began to lose ground.
Today the majority of Brazilian Zouk students are young, educated and social network-savvy. The essential street-wise /beach-based/ sassy / extroverted / fast-paced/ sexually polarized elements of classic Lambada have morphed into the now popular and more physically conservative/ androgynous / lyrical / introverted/ trancy forms. And what was intuitive, innate and natural has, in some settings, become far more stylized and the subject of endless verbal analysis. But donâ€™t get me wrong - many beautiful and interesting styles of dance have developed from Lambada, though, and some superb performers and teachers have emerged. And one can only admire the ability of leaders in those fields to engage students as they have done.
These days, Lambada is enjoying a resurgence in the United States and elsewhere, and its original name has been reclaimed. Brazilian Zouk Dancers are interested in exploring more variety in terms of dance â€˜energiaâ€™ - and it is noteworthy that Brazilian Zouk Jack & Jill competitions in Northern America now comprise a faster section.
There are considerable challenges involved in dancing Lambada well - including the need for heightened musicality at fast tempo, the ability to swap partners and dance with more than one person at a time, extraordinary athleticism, and an acutely exquisite partner connection even without physical touch. Nevertheless, today die-hard Lambadeiros and â€˜Lambaâ€™ newcomers alike bask in the pure pleasure of their extraordinary dance, and hungrily seek its fun and potency wherever they can.
For those who have so far been exposed only to more contemporary forms of Lambada - acknowledging the roots of Brazilian Zouk is not only ethically essential; the truth is that understanding the basic forms and patterns of classic Lambada leads to a far better ability to understand and execute Brazilian Zouk. It is no mistake that some of the innovators of new styles - AdÃ­lio Porto and Renato Veronezi for example - were originally
fantastic classical lambadeiros.
It seems smart and logical that those who started with Brazilian Zouk should be trying to learn classic Lambada as well, right? After all, its of similar importance as learning Classical Ballet first before attempting Modern Ballet...
And for those of you for whom learning the roots of your dance seems out of reach or too hard, at least take comfort in knowing that- as a Brazilian Zouker - you ALREADY dance Lambada.

Zouklove is danced to slower music and it is a more dramatic and sensual style of Zouk. Zouklove has its origins in a slow tempo form of cadence sung by Ophelia Marie of the Dominica. Zouklove in turn influenced an African genre of Zouk called Kizomba which developed in Angola and Cape Verde.	https://youtu.be/pAiORfHqTfY

[[Zouk Phrasing]]
[[RnB rhythm in Zouk]]

In music we often count only Up beats.

In dance we usually count also downbeats. And in order to give it some proper numbers that we can define, we often make it twice slower, so it is easier to define, where we step.

# Zouk.md

---
type: dance
---


Zouk is a dance, it is not a music (as with [[tango argentino]] for example). That is why it is always developing, because it doesn't have fixed borders. It is influenced by the music it is danced on. Zouk will never stop developing because the music will never stop it. 
[[Alex Carvalho]]
